<p><b>Sir Alexander Chapman</b> "<b>Alex</b>" <b>Ferguson</b>, <small><a href="/wiki/Order_of_the_British_Empire" title="Order of the British Empire">CBE</a></small> (born 31 December 1941) is a former Scottish <a href="/wiki/Manager_(association_football)" title="Manager (association football)">football manager</a> and <a href="/wiki/Football_player" title="Football player">player</a> who managed <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C." title="Manchester United F.C.">Manchester United</a> from 1986 to 2013. He is regarded by many players, managers and analysts to be one of the greatest and most successful managers of all time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>Ferguson played as a <a href="/wiki/Forward_(association_football)" title="Forward (association football)">forward</a> for several Scottish clubs, including <a href="/wiki/Dunfermline_Athletic_F.C." title="Dunfermline Athletic F.C.">Dunfermline Athletic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rangers_F.C." title="Rangers F.C.">Rangers</a>. While playing for Dunfermline, he was the top goalscorer in the Scottish league in the <a href="/wiki/1965%E2%80%9366_in_Scottish_football" title="1965–66 in Scottish football">1965–66</a> season. Towards the end of his playing career he also worked as a coach, then started his managerial career with <a href="/wiki/East_Stirlingshire_F.C." title="East Stirlingshire F.C.">East Stirlingshire</a> and <a href="/wiki/St_Mirren_F.C." title="St Mirren F.C.">St Mirren</a>. Ferguson then enjoyed a highly successful period as manager of <a href="/wiki/Aberdeen_F.C." title="Aberdeen F.C.">Aberdeen</a>, winning three Scottish league championships, four <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Cup" title="Scottish Cup">Scottish Cups</a> and the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Cup_Winners%27_Cup" title="UEFA Cup Winners' Cup">UEFA Cup Winners' Cup</a> in <a href="/wiki/1982%E2%80%9383_European_Cup_Winners%27_Cup" title="1982–83 European Cup Winners' Cup">1983</a>. He briefly managed <a href="/wiki/Scotland_national_football_team" title="Scotland national football team">Scotland</a> following the death of <a href="/wiki/Jock_Stein" title="Jock Stein">Jock Stein</a>, taking the team to the <a href="/wiki/1986_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1986 FIFA World Cup">1986 World Cup</a>.</p>
<p>Ferguson was appointed manager of <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C." title="Manchester United F.C.">Manchester United</a> in November 1986. During his 26 years with Manchester United he won 38 trophies, including 13 <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a> titles, five <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup" title="FA Cup">FA Cups</a> and two <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">UEFA Champions League</a> titles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-retirement_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-retirement-8">[8]</a></sup> He was knighted in the <a href="/wiki/1999_Birthday_Honours" title="1999 Birthday Honours">1999 Queen's Birthday Honours</a> list, for his services to the game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> Ferguson is the longest serving manager of Manchester United, having overtaken <a href="/wiki/Matt_Busby" title="Matt Busby">Sir Matt Busby</a>'s record on 19 December 2010. He retired from management at the end of the 2012–13 season, having won the Premier League in his final season.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span></h2>
<p>Born to Alexander Beaton Ferguson, a plater's helper in the shipbuilding industry, and his wife, Elizabeth (née Hardie),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> Alex Ferguson was born at his grandmother's home on Shieldhall Road, <a href="/wiki/Govan" title="Govan">Govan</a>, on 31 December 1941, but grew up in a tenement at 667 Govan Road (which has since been demolished) where he lived with his parents as well as his younger brother <a href="/wiki/Martin_Ferguson_(footballer)" title="Martin Ferguson (footballer)">Martin</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p>He attended <a href="/wiki/Broomloan_Road_Primary_School" title="Broomloan Road Primary School">Broomloan Road Primary School</a> and later <a href="/wiki/Govan_High_School" title="Govan High School">Govan High School</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> and supported <a href="/wiki/Rangers_F.C." title="Rangers F.C.">Rangers</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Playing_career">Playing career</span></h2>
<p>Ferguson's playing career began as an amateur with <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_Park_F.C." title="Queen's Park F.C.">Queen's Park</a>, where he made his debut as a <a href="/wiki/Forward_(association_football)" title="Forward (association football)">striker</a> aged 16.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> He described his first match as a "nightmare",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nightmare_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-nightmare-16">[16]</a></sup> but scored Queen's Park's goal in a 2–1 defeat against <a href="/wiki/Stranraer_F.C." title="Stranraer F.C.">Stranraer</a>. Perhaps his most notable game for Queen's Park was the 7–1 defeat away to <a href="/wiki/Queen_of_the_South_F.C." title="Queen of the South F.C.">Queen of the South</a> on <a href="/wiki/Boxing_Day" title="Boxing Day">Boxing Day</a> 1959 when ex-England international <a href="/wiki/Ivor_Broadis" title="Ivor Broadis">Ivor Broadis</a> scored four of the Queen of the South goals. Ferguson was the solitary Queen's Park goalscorer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>Despite scoring 20 <a href="/wiki/Goal_(sport)" title="Goal (sport)">goals</a> in his 31 games for Queen's Park, he could not command a regular place in the side and moved to <a href="/wiki/St_Johnstone_F.C." title="St Johnstone F.C.">St Johnstone</a> in 1960. Although he continued to score regularly at St Johnstone, he was still unable to command a regular place and regularly requested transfers. Ferguson was out of favour at the club and he even considered emigrating to Canada,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> however St Johnstone's failure to sign a forward led the manager to select Ferguson for a match against Rangers, in which he scored a <a href="/wiki/Hat-trick" title="Hat-trick">hat-trick</a> in a surprise victory. <a href="/wiki/Dunfermline_Athletic_F.C." title="Dunfermline Athletic F.C.">Dunfermline</a> signed him the following summer (1964), and Ferguson became a full-time professional footballer.</p>
<p>The following season (<a href="/wiki/1964%E2%80%9365_in_Scottish_football" title="1964–65 in Scottish football">1964–65</a>), Dunfermline were strong challengers for the Scottish League and reached the Scottish Cup Final, but Ferguson was dropped for the final after a poor performance in a league game against St Johnstone. Dunfermline lost the final 3–2 to Celtic, then failed to win the League by one point. The <a href="/wiki/1965%E2%80%9366_in_Scottish_football" title="1965–66 in Scottish football">1965–66</a> season saw Ferguson notch up 45 goals in 51 games for Dunfermline. Along with <a href="/wiki/Joe_McBride_(footballer,_born_1938)" title="Joe McBride (footballer, born 1938)">Joe McBride</a> of Celtic, he was the top goalscorer in the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Premier_League" title="Scottish Premier League">Scottish League</a> with 31 goals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<p>He then joined Rangers for £65,000, then a record fee for a transfer between two Scottish clubs. He was blamed for a goal that they conceded in the <a href="/wiki/1968%E2%80%9369_Scottish_Cup#Final" title="1968–69 Scottish Cup">1969 Scottish Cup Final</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-blame_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-blame-20">[20]</a></sup> in a match in which he was designated to mark <a href="/wiki/Celtic_F.C." title="Celtic F.C.">Celtic</a> <a href="/wiki/Captain_(association_football)" title="Captain (association football)">captain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Billy_McNeill" title="Billy McNeill">Billy McNeill</a>, and was subsequently forced to play for the club's junior side instead of for the first team.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-junior_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-junior-21">[21]</a></sup> According to his brother, Ferguson was so upset by the experience that he threw his losers' medal away.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-losersmedal_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-losersmedal-22">[22]</a></sup> There have been claims that he suffered discrimination at Rangers after his marriage to a Catholic, Cathy Holding,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> but Ferguson himself makes it clear in his autobiography<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> that Rangers knew of his wife's religion when he joined the club and that he left the club very reluctantly, due to the fall-out from his alleged cup final mistake.</p>
<p>The following October, <a href="/wiki/Nottingham_Forest_F.C." title="Nottingham Forest F.C.">Nottingham Forest</a> wanted to sign Ferguson,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-signforest_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-signforest-25">[25]</a></sup> but his wife was not keen on moving to England at that time so he went to <a href="/wiki/Falkirk_F.C." title="Falkirk F.C.">Falkirk</a> instead. He was promoted to player-coach there, but when <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_Prentice_(footballer_born_1926)" title="John Prentice (footballer born 1926)">John Prentice</a> became manager he removed Ferguson's coaching responsibilities. Ferguson responded by requesting a transfer and moved to <a href="/wiki/Ayr_United_F.C." title="Ayr United F.C.">Ayr United</a>, where he finished his playing career in 1974.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_managerial_career">Early managerial career</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="East_Stirlingshire">East Stirlingshire</span></h3>
<p>In June 1974, Ferguson was appointed manager of <a href="/wiki/East_Stirlingshire_F.C." title="East Stirlingshire F.C.">East Stirlingshire</a>, at the comparatively young age of 32. It was a part-time job that paid £40 per week, and the club did not have a single <a href="/wiki/Goalkeeper_(association_football)" title="Goalkeeper (association football)">goalkeeper</a> at the time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-boss108-9_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-boss108-9-26">[26]</a></sup> He gained a reputation as a disciplinarian, with club forward <a href="/wiki/Bobby_McCulley" title="Bobby McCulley">Bobby McCulley</a> later saying he had "never been afraid of anyone before but Ferguson was a frightening bastard from the start."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bastard_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-bastard-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<p>The following October, Ferguson was invited to manage <a href="/wiki/St_Mirren_F.C." title="St Mirren F.C.">St Mirren</a>. While they were below <a href="/wiki/East_Stirlingshire_F.C." title="East Stirlingshire F.C.">East Stirlingshire</a> in the league, they were a bigger club and although Ferguson felt a degree of loyalty towards East Stirlingshire, he decided to join St Mirren after taking advice from <a href="/wiki/Jock_Stein" title="Jock Stein">Jock Stein</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-boss117_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-boss117-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="St_Mirren">St Mirren</span></h3>
<p>Ferguson was manager of St Mirren from 1974 until 1978, producing a remarkable transformation of a team in the lower half of the old <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Football_League_Second_Division" title="Scottish Football League Second Division">Second Division</a> watched by crowds of just over 1,000, to <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Football_League_First_Division" title="Scottish Football League First Division">First Division</a> champions in <a href="/wiki/1976%E2%80%9377_in_Scottish_football" title="1976–77 in Scottish football">1977</a>, discovering talent like <a href="/wiki/Billy_Stark" title="Billy Stark">Billy Stark</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tony_Fitzpatrick_(footballer)" title="Tony Fitzpatrick (footballer)">Tony Fitzpatrick</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lex_Richardson" title="Lex Richardson">Lex Richardson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frank_McGarvey" title="Frank McGarvey">Frank McGarvey</a>, Bobby Reid and <a href="/wiki/Peter_Weir_(footballer)" title="Peter Weir (footballer)">Peter Weir</a> while playing superb attacking football.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sunday_Herald_St_Mirren_article_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sunday_Herald_St_Mirren_article-29">[29]</a></sup> The average age of the league winning team was 19 and the captain, Fitzpatrick, was 20.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FA_article_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-FA_article-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<p>St Mirren have the distinction of being the only club ever to sack Ferguson. He claimed wrongful dismissal against the club at an industrial tribunal but lost and was given no leave to appeal. According to a Billy Adams <i><a href="/wiki/Sunday_Herald" title="Sunday Herald">Sunday Herald</a></i> article on 30 May 1999, the official version is that Ferguson was sacked for various breaches of contract including unauthorised payments to players.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sunday_Herald_St_Mirren_article_29-1"><a href="#cite_note-Sunday_Herald_St_Mirren_article-29">[29]</a></sup> He was counter-accused of intimidating behaviour towards his office secretary because he wanted players to get some expenses tax free. He did not speak to her for six weeks, confiscated her keys and communicated only through a 17-year-old assistant. The tribunal concluded that Ferguson was "particularly petty" and "immature".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guardian_bullying_article_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian_bullying_article-31">[31]</a></sup> It was claimed during the tribunal by St Mirren chairman, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Willie_Todd&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Willie Todd (page does not exist)">Willie Todd</a>, that Ferguson had "no managerial ability".</p>
<p>On 31 May 2008, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> published an interview with Todd (then aged 87), who had sacked Ferguson many years earlier. Todd explained that the fundamental reason for the dismissal was a breach of contract relating to Ferguson having agreed to join Aberdeen. Ferguson told journalist Jim Rodger of the <i><a href="/wiki/Daily_Mirror" title="Daily Mirror">Daily Mirror</a></i> that he had asked at least one member of the squad to go to Aberdeen with him. He told the St Mirren staff he was leaving. Todd expressed regret over what happened but blamed Aberdeen for not approaching his club to discuss compensation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1977, Ferguson turned down the manager's job at Aberdeen. The role went to <a href="/wiki/Billy_McNeill" title="Billy McNeill">Billy McNeill</a>, who returned to Celtic after only a year, leaving the role available for Ferguson once again.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Aberdeen">Aberdeen</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Late_1970s">Late 1970s</span></h3>
<p>Ferguson joined Aberdeen as manager in June 1978, replacing <a href="/wiki/Billy_McNeill" title="Billy McNeill">Billy McNeill</a> who had only managed the club for one season before he was offered the chance to manage Celtic. Although Aberdeen were one of Scotland's major clubs they had won the league only once, in <a href="/wiki/1954%E2%80%9355_in_Scottish_football" title="1954–55 in Scottish football">1955</a> under <a href="/wiki/Dave_Halliday" title="Dave Halliday">Dave Halliday</a>. The team had been playing well, however, and had not lost a league match since the previous December, having finished second in the league the previous season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-boss159_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-boss159-34">[34]</a></sup> Ferguson had now been a manager for four years, but was still not much older than some of the players and had trouble winning the respect of some of the older ones such as <a href="/wiki/Joe_Harper" title="Joe Harper">Joe Harper</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-boss171_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-boss171-35">[35]</a></sup> The season did not go especially well, with Aberdeen reaching the semi-final of the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Cup" title="Scottish Cup">Scottish Cup</a> and the <a href="/wiki/1979_Scottish_League_Cup_Final_(March)" title="1979 Scottish League Cup Final (March)">Scottish League Cup Final</a>, but losing both matches and finishing fourth in the league.</p>
<p>Aberdeen lost the <a href="/wiki/1979_Scottish_League_Cup_Final_(December)" title="1979 Scottish League Cup Final (December)">1979–80 Scottish League Cup Final</a>, this time to <a href="/wiki/Dundee_United_F.C." title="Dundee United F.C.">Dundee United</a> after a replay. Ferguson took the blame for the defeat, saying he should have made changes to the team for the replay.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-boss174_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-boss174-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1980s_and_silverware">1980s and silverware</span></h3>
<p>Aberdeen had started the <a href="/wiki/1979%E2%80%9380_Scottish_Football_League" title="1979–80 Scottish Football League">1979–80 season</a> poorly but their form improved dramatically in the new year and they won the Scottish league that season with a 5–0 win on the final day. It was the first time in 15 years that the league had not been won by either Rangers or Celtic. Ferguson now felt that he had the respect of his players, later saying "That was the achievement which united us. I finally had the players believing in me".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-boss175_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-boss175-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<p>He was still a strict disciplinarian, though, and his players nicknamed him "Furious Fergie". He fined one of his players, <a href="/wiki/John_Hewitt_(footballer)" title="John Hewitt (footballer)">John Hewitt</a>, for overtaking him on a public road,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-boss179_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-boss179-38">[38]</a></sup> and kicked a tea urn at the players at half time after a poor first half.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-boss180_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-boss180-39">[39]</a></sup> He was dissatisfied with the atmosphere at Aberdeen matches, and deliberately created a "<a href="/wiki/Siege_mentality" title="Siege mentality">siege mentality</a>" by accusing the Scottish media of being biased towards the Glasgow clubs, to motivate the team.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-boss191_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-boss191-40">[40]</a></sup> The team continued their success with a Scottish Cup win in 1982. Ferguson was offered the manager's job at <a href="/wiki/Wolverhampton_Wanderers_F.C." title="Wolverhampton Wanderers F.C.">Wolverhampton Wanderers</a> but turned it down as he felt that Wolves were in trouble<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-boss195_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-boss195-41">[41]</a></sup> and "[his] ambitions at Aberdeen were not even half fulfilled".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-boss196_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-boss196-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="European_success">European success</span></h3>
<p>Ferguson led Aberdeen to even greater success the following season, 1982–83. They had qualified for the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Cup_Winners%27_Cup" title="UEFA Cup Winners' Cup">European Cup Winners' Cup</a> as a result of winning the Scottish Cup the previous season, and impressively knocked out <a href="/wiki/FC_Bayern_Munich" title="FC Bayern Munich">Bayern Munich</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> who had beaten <a href="/wiki/Tottenham_Hotspur_F.C." title="Tottenham Hotspur F.C.">Tottenham Hotspur</a> 4–1 in the previous round.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/Willie_Miller" title="Willie Miller">Willie Miller</a>, this gave them the confidence to believe that they could go on to win the competition,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-boss201_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-boss201-47">[47]</a></sup> which they did, with a 2–1 victory over <a href="/wiki/Real_Madrid_C.F." title="Real Madrid C.F.">Real Madrid</a> in the final on 11 May 1983.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> Aberdeen became only the third Scottish team to win a European trophy and Ferguson now felt that "he'd done something worthwhile with his life".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-boss203_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-boss203-49">[49]</a></sup> This was followed up with victory in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_Super_Cup" title="European Super Cup">European Super Cup</a> in December 1983, when <a href="/wiki/Hamburger_SV" title="Hamburger SV">Hamburger SV</a>, the reigning <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">European Cup</a> champions, were beaten 2–0 over two legs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> Aberdeen had also performed well in the league that season, and retained the Scottish Cup with a 1–0 victory over Rangers,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> but Ferguson was not happy with his team's play in that match and upset the players by describing theirs as a "disgraceful performance" in a televised interview after the match, a statement he later retracted.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-boss204_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-boss204-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<p>After a sub-standard start to the <a href="/wiki/1983%E2%80%9384_in_Scottish_football" title="1983–84 in Scottish football">1983–84 season</a>, Aberdeen's form improved and the team won the Scottish league and retained the Scottish Cup. Ferguson was appointed an Officer of the <a href="/wiki/Order_of_the_British_Empire" title="Order of the British Empire">Order of the British Empire</a> (OBE) in the <a href="/wiki/1985_New_Year_Honours" title="1985 New Year Honours">1985 New Year Honours</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OBE_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-OBE-54">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> and was offered the managers' jobs at Rangers and <a href="/wiki/Arsenal_F.C." title="Arsenal F.C.">Arsenal</a> during the season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> Aberdeen retained their league title in the 1984–85 season, but had a disappointing season in 1985–86, finishing fourth in the league, although they did win both domestic cups. Ferguson had been appointed to the club's board of directors early in 1986, but that April he told Dick Donald, their chairman, that he intended to leave that summer.</p>
<p>Ferguson had been part of coaching staff for the <a href="/wiki/Scotland_national_football_team" title="Scotland national football team">Scottish national side</a> during qualifying for the <a href="/wiki/1986_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1986 FIFA World Cup">1986 World Cup</a>, but manager <a href="/wiki/Jock_Stein" title="Jock Stein">Jock Stein</a> had <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1985_Wales_vs_Scotland_football_match" title="1985 Wales vs Scotland football match">collapsed and died on 10 September 1985</a> – at the end of the game in which Scotland qualified from their group for a play-off against <a href="/wiki/Australia_national_soccer_team" title="Australia national soccer team">Australia</a>. Ferguson promptly agreed to take charge of the Scottish national side against the Australians and subsequently at the World Cup. To allow him to fulfil his international duties he appointed <a href="/wiki/Archie_Knox" title="Archie Knox">Archie Knox</a> as his co-manager at Aberdeen. However, after Scotland failed to progress past the group stages of the World Cup, Ferguson stepped down as national team manager on 15 June 1986.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup></p>
<p>Around this time, Tottenham Hotspur offered Ferguson the chance to take over from <a href="/wiki/Peter_Shreeves" title="Peter Shreeves">Peter Shreeves</a> as manager, but he rejected this offer and the job went to <a href="/wiki/Luton_Town_F.C." title="Luton Town F.C.">Luton Town's</a> <a href="/wiki/David_Pleat" title="David Pleat">David Pleat</a> instead. There was also an offer for Ferguson to replace <a href="/wiki/Don_Howe" title="Don Howe">Don Howe</a> as Arsenal manager, but he rejected this offer as well, and fellow Scot <a href="/wiki/George_Graham_(footballer)" title="George Graham (footballer)">George Graham</a> took the post instead.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> That summer, there had been speculation that he would take over from <a href="/wiki/Ron_Atkinson" title="Ron Atkinson">Ron Atkinson</a> at <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C." title="Manchester United F.C.">Manchester United</a>, who had slumped to fourth in the English top flight after a ten-match winning start had made title glory seem inevitable.</p>
<p>It was not the first time that Ferguson had been linked with a move to England. In February 1982, Wolverhampton Wanderers had approached him about succeeding <a href="/wiki/John_Barnwell" title="John Barnwell">John Barnwell</a> as manager as they were heading for relegation from the First Division.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> He rejected this offer, perhaps concerned about the club's financial stability, as they were more than £2 million in debt at the time and narrowly avoided going out of business. At the end of the 1984–85 season, it was reported that Ferguson was being considered for the <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool</a> manager's job after the retirement of <a href="/wiki/Joe_Fagan" title="Joe Fagan">Joe Fagan</a> was announced, but the job was quickly accepted by Liverpool striker <a href="/wiki/Kenny_Dalglish" title="Kenny Dalglish">Kenny Dalglish</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<p>Although Ferguson remained at Aberdeen over the summer, he did eventually join Manchester United when Atkinson was sacked in November 1986.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Manchester_United">Manchester United</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Appointment_and_first_years">Appointment and first years</span></h3>
<p>Ferguson was appointed manager at <a href="/wiki/Old_Trafford" title="Old Trafford">Old Trafford</a> on 6 November 1986. He was initially worried that many of the players, such as <a href="/wiki/Norman_Whiteside" title="Norman Whiteside">Norman Whiteside</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paul_McGrath_(footballer)" title="Paul McGrath (footballer)">Paul McGrath</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bryan_Robson" title="Bryan Robson">Bryan Robson</a> were drinking too much and was "depressed" by their level of fitness, but he managed to increase the players' discipline and United climbed up the table to finish the season in 11th place, having been 21st (second from bottom) when he took over.</p>
<p>His first game in charge was a 2–0 defeat at <a href="/wiki/Oxford_United_F.C." title="Oxford United F.C.">Oxford United</a> on 8 November, followed seven days later by a goalless draw at newly promoted <a href="/wiki/Norwich_City_F.C." title="Norwich City F.C.">Norwich City</a>, and then his first win (1–0 at home to <a href="/wiki/Queens_Park_Rangers_F.C." title="Queens Park Rangers F.C.">Queens Park Rangers</a>) on 22 November. Results steadily improved as the season went on, and by the time they recorded what would be their only away win of the league campaign at title challengers and deadly rivals Liverpool on <a href="/wiki/Boxing_Day" title="Boxing Day">Boxing Day</a>, it was clear that United were on the road to recovery. 1987 began on a high note with a 4–1 victory over <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_United_F.C." title="Newcastle United F.C.">Newcastle United</a> and United gradually pulled together in the second half of the season, with relatively occasional defeats on the way, and finished 11th in the final table. Ferguson's mother Elizabeth died of lung cancer, aged 64, three weeks after his appointment. Ferguson appointed <a href="/wiki/Archie_Knox" title="Archie Knox">Archie Knox</a>, his assistant at Aberdeen, as his assistant at Manchester United in 1986.</p>
<p>In the 1987–88 season, Ferguson made several major signings, including <a href="/wiki/Steve_Bruce" title="Steve Bruce">Steve Bruce</a>, <a href="/wiki/Viv_Anderson" title="Viv Anderson">Viv Anderson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brian_McClair" title="Brian McClair">Brian McClair</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jim_Leighton" title="Jim Leighton">Jim Leighton</a>. The new players made a great contribution to a United team who finished in second place, nine points behind Liverpool. Liverpool's points lead, however, had been in double digits for most of the season and while United had lost only five league games all season, they drew 12 games and there was clearly still some way to go before United could be a match for their north western rivals.</p>
<p>During the season, United played two friendly matches in Bermuda against the <a href="/wiki/Bermuda_national_football_team" title="Bermuda national football team">Bermuda national team</a> and the Somerset Cricket Club.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bermuda_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-bermuda-64">[64]</a></sup> In the match against Somerset, both Ferguson himself and his assistant, Archie Knox, took to the field, with Knox even getting on the scoresheet. The match was Ferguson's only appearance for the Manchester United first team.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bermuda_64-1"><a href="#cite_note-bermuda-64">[64]</a></sup></p>
<p>United were expected to do well when <a href="/wiki/Mark_Hughes" title="Mark Hughes">Mark Hughes</a> returned to the club two years after leaving for <a href="/wiki/FC_Barcelona" title="FC Barcelona">Barcelona</a>, but the <a href="/wiki/1988%E2%80%9389_Manchester_United_F.C._season" title="1988–89 Manchester United F.C. season">1988–89 season</a> was a disappointment for them, finishing 11th in the league and losing 1–0 at home to Nottingham Forest in the <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup" title="FA Cup">FA Cup</a> <a href="/wiki/1988%E2%80%9389_FA_Cup" title="1988–89 FA Cup">Sixth Round</a>. They had begun the season slowly, going on a nine-match winless run throughout October and November (with one defeat and eight draws) before a run of generally good results took them to third place and the fringes of the title challenge by mid February. However, another run of disappointing results in the final quarter of the season saw them fall down to mid-table.</p>
<p>For the <a href="/wiki/1989%E2%80%9390_Manchester_United_F.C._season" title="1989–90 Manchester United F.C. season">1989–90 season</a>, Ferguson further boosted his squad by paying large sums of money for midfielders <a href="/wiki/Neil_Webb" title="Neil Webb">Neil Webb</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mike_Phelan" title="Mike Phelan">Mike Phelan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Paul_Ince" title="Paul Ince">Paul Ince</a>, as well as defender <a href="/wiki/Gary_Pallister" title="Gary Pallister">Gary Pallister</a> and winger <a href="/wiki/Danny_Wallace_(footballer)" title="Danny Wallace (footballer)">Danny Wallace</a>. The season began well with a 4–1 win over defending champions Arsenal on the opening day, but United's league form quickly turned sour. In September, United suffered a humiliating 5–1 away defeat against <a href="/wiki/Manchester_derby" title="Manchester derby">fierce rivals</a> <a href="/wiki/Manchester_City_F.C." title="Manchester City F.C.">Manchester City</a>. Following this and an early season run of six defeats and two draws in eight games, a banner declaring, "Three years of excuses and it's still crap ... ta-ra Fergie." was displayed at Old Trafford, and many journalists and supporters called for Ferguson to be sacked.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3years_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-3years-65">[65]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> Ferguson later described December 1989 as "the darkest period [he had] ever suffered in the game", as United ended the decade just outside the relegation zone.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jc27_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-jc27-68">[68]</a></sup></p>
<p>Ferguson, however, later revealed that the board of directors had assured him that they were not considering dismissing him. Although naturally disappointed with the lack of success in the league, they understood the reasons for the sub-standard results (namely the absence of several key players due to injury) and were pleased with the way that Ferguson had reorganised the club's coaching and scouting system.</p>
<p>Following a run of seven games without a win, Manchester United were drawn away to Nottingham Forest in the third round of the FA Cup. Forest were performing well that season and were in the process of winning the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Football_League_Cup" title="Football League Cup">League Cup</a> for the second season running,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Robins_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-Robins-69">[69]</a></sup> and it was expected that United would lose the match and Ferguson would consequently be sacked, but United won the game 1–0 due to a <a href="/wiki/Mark_Robins" title="Mark Robins">Mark Robins</a> goal and eventually reached the final. This cup win is often cited as the match that saved Ferguson's Old Trafford career, even though it has since been stated that his job was never at risk.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Robins_69-1"><a href="#cite_note-Robins-69">[69]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20years_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-20years-70">[70]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pressure_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-Pressure-71">[71]</a></sup> United went on to win the FA Cup, beating <a href="/wiki/Crystal_Palace_F.C." title="Crystal Palace F.C.">Crystal Palace</a> 1–0 in the final replay after a 3–3 draw in the first match, giving Ferguson his first major trophy as Manchester United manager. United's defensive frailties in the first match were unilaterally blamed on goalkeeper Jim Leighton, forcing Ferguson to drop his former Aberdeen player and bring in <a href="/wiki/Les_Sealey" title="Les Sealey">Les Sealey</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_first_league_title">The first league title</span></h3>
<p>Although United's league form improved greatly in <a href="/wiki/1990%E2%80%9391_Manchester_United_F.C._season" title="1990–91 Manchester United F.C. season">1990–91</a>, they were still inconsistent and finished sixth. There were some excellent performances that season, including a 6–2 demolition of Arsenal at <a href="/wiki/Arsenal_Stadium" title="Arsenal Stadium">Highbury</a>, but results like an early 2–1 loss at newly promoted <a href="/wiki/Sunderland_A.F.C." title="Sunderland A.F.C.">Sunderland</a>, a 4–0 September hammering by Liverpool at Anfield, and a 2–0 home defeat by <a href="/wiki/Everton_F.C." title="Everton F.C.">Everton</a> in early March (the game where 17-year-old hot prospect <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Giggs" title="Ryan Giggs">Ryan Giggs</a> made his senior debut) showed that United still had some way to go.</p>
<p>Even after the FA Cup final victory in the previous season, some still had doubts about Ferguson's ability to succeed where all the other managers since <a href="/wiki/Matt_Busby" title="Matt Busby">Matt Busby</a> had failed – to win the league title.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pressure_71-1"><a href="#cite_note-Pressure-71">[71]</a></sup> They were runners-up in the <a href="/wiki/1991_Football_League_Cup_Final" title="1991 Football League Cup Final">League Cup</a>, losing 1–0 to <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Wednesday_F.C." title="Sheffield Wednesday F.C.">Sheffield Wednesday</a>. They also reached the final of the <a href="/wiki/1991_European_Cup_Winners%27_Cup_Final" title="1991 European Cup Winners' Cup Final">European Cup Winners' Cup</a>, beating that season's Spanish champions Barcelona 2–1. After the match, Ferguson vowed that United would win the league the following season, and at long last he seemed to have won over the last of his sceptics after nearly five years in the job.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mml302_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-mml302-72">[72]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the 1991 close season, Ferguson's assistant Archie Knox departed to Rangers to become assistant to <a href="/wiki/Walter_Smith" title="Walter Smith">Walter Smith</a>, and Ferguson promoted youth team coach <a href="/wiki/Brian_Kidd" title="Brian Kidd">Brian Kidd</a> to the role of assistant manager in Knox's place. He also made two major signings – goalkeeper <a href="/wiki/Peter_Schmeichel" title="Peter Schmeichel">Peter Schmeichel</a> and defender <a href="/wiki/Paul_Parker_(footballer)" title="Paul Parker (footballer)">Paul Parker</a> – to bolster his side. There was much anticipation about the breakthrough of the young Ryan Giggs, who had played twice and scored once in the 1990–91 campaign, and the earlier emergence of another impressive young winger in the shape of <a href="/wiki/Lee_Sharpe" title="Lee Sharpe">Lee Sharpe</a>, who despite their youth had made Ferguson feel able to resist plunging into the transfer market and buying a new player to take over from the disappointing Danny Wallace on the left wing. He had also added the <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukrainian</a> <a href="/wiki/Andrei_Kanchelskis" title="Andrei Kanchelskis">Andrei Kanchelskis</a> to the right wing, giving him a more attacking alternative to older right footed midfielders <a href="/wiki/Mike_Phelan" title="Mike Phelan">Mike Phelan</a> and Bryan Robson.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/1991%E2%80%9392_Manchester_United_F.C._season" title="1991–92 Manchester United F.C. season">1991–92 season</a> did not live up to Ferguson's expectations and, in Ferguson's words, "many in the media felt that [his] mistakes had contributed to the misery".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mml311_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-mml311-73">[73]</a></sup> United won the <a href="/wiki/1991%E2%80%9392_Football_League_Cup" title="1991–92 Football League Cup">League Cup</a> and <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Super_Cup" title="UEFA Super Cup">UEFA Super Cup</a> for the first time, but lost out on the <a href="/wiki/1991%E2%80%9392_Football_League#First_Division_2" title="1991–92 Football League">league title</a> to rivals <a href="/wiki/Leeds_United_F.C." title="Leeds United F.C.">Leeds United</a> after leading the table for much of the season. A shortage of goals and being held to draws by teams they had been expected to beat in the second half of the campaign had proved to be the undoing of a United side who had performed so well in the first half of the season. Ferguson felt that his failure to secure the signing of <a href="/wiki/Mick_Harford" title="Mick Harford">Mick Harford</a> from <a href="/wiki/Luton_Town_F.C." title="Luton Town F.C.">Luton Town</a> had cost United the league, and that he needed "an extra dimension" to the team if they were to win the league the following season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mml320_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-mml320-74">[74]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the 1992 close season, Ferguson went on the hunt for a new striker. He first attempted to sign <a href="/wiki/Alan_Shearer" title="Alan Shearer">Alan Shearer</a> from <a href="/wiki/Southampton_F.C." title="Southampton F.C.">Southampton</a>, but lost out to <a href="/wiki/Blackburn_Rovers_F.C." title="Blackburn Rovers F.C.">Blackburn Rovers</a>. He also made at least one approach for the Sheffield Wednesday striker <a href="/wiki/David_Hirst_(footballer)" title="David Hirst (footballer)">David Hirst</a>, but manager <a href="/wiki/Trevor_Francis" title="Trevor Francis">Trevor Francis</a> rejected all offers and the player stayed put. In the end, he paid £1 million for 23-year-old <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_United_F.C." title="Cambridge United F.C.">Cambridge United</a> striker <a href="/wiki/Dion_Dublin" title="Dion Dublin">Dion Dublin</a> – his only major signing of the summer.</p>
<p>After a slow start to the <a href="/wiki/1992%E2%80%9393_Manchester_United_F.C._season" title="1992–93 Manchester United F.C. season">1992–93 season</a> (they were 10th of 22 at the beginning of November) it looked as though United would miss out on the league title (now the <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a>) yet again. However, after the purchase of French striker <a href="/wiki/Eric_Cantona" title="Eric Cantona">Eric Cantona</a> from Leeds for £1.2 million, the future of Manchester United, and Ferguson's position as manager, began to look bright. Cantona formed a strong partnership with Mark Hughes and fired the club to the top of the table, ending United's 26-year wait for a League Championship, and also making them the first ever <a href="/wiki/List_of_English_football_champions#Premier_League_.281992.E2.80.93present.29" title="List of English football champions">Premier League Champions</a>. United had finished champions with a ten-point margin over runners-up <a href="/wiki/Aston_Villa_F.C." title="Aston Villa F.C.">Aston Villa</a>, whose 1–0 defeat at <a href="/wiki/Oldham_Athletic_A.F.C." title="Oldham Athletic A.F.C.">Oldham Athletic</a> on 2 May 1993 had given United the title. Ferguson was voted Manager of the Year by the League Managers' Association.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1993.E2.80.9395:_Double_win_and_loss">1993–95: Double win and loss</span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/1993%E2%80%9394_Manchester_United_F.C._season" title="1993–94 Manchester United F.C. season">1993–94 season</a> brought more success. Ferguson added Nottingham Forest's 22-year-old midfielder <a href="/wiki/Roy_Keane" title="Roy Keane">Roy Keane</a> to the ranks for a British record fee of £3.75 million as a long term replacement for Bryan Robson, who was nearing the end of his career.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup></p>
<p>United led the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1993%E2%80%9394_Premier_League" title="1993–94 Premier League">1993–94 Premier League</a> table virtually from start to finish.</p>
<p>Ferguson was the very first winner of the <a href="/wiki/Premier_League_Manager_of_the_Month" title="Premier League Manager of the Month">Premier League Manager of the Month</a> award, introduced for the start of the 1993–94 season, when he collected the accolade for August 1993.</p>
<p>Cantona was top scorer with 25 goals in all competitions despite being <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Foul_(association_football)" title="Foul (association football)">sent off</a> twice in the space of five days in March 1994. United also reached the League Cup final but lost 3–1 to Aston Villa, managed by Ferguson's predecessor, Ron Atkinson. In the FA Cup final, Manchester United achieved an impressive 4–0 scoreline against <a href="/wiki/Chelsea_F.C." title="Chelsea F.C.">Chelsea</a>, winning Ferguson his second <a href="/wiki/Double_(association_football)#England" title="Double (association football)">League and Cup Double</a>, following his Scottish Premier Division and Scottish Cup titles with Aberdeen in 1984–85, though the League Cup final defeat meant that he had not yet achieved a repeat of the treble that he had achieved with Aberdeen in 1983.</p>
<p>Ferguson made only one close-season signing, paying Blackburn £1.2 million for <a href="/wiki/David_May_(footballer)" title="David May (footballer)">David May</a>. There were newspaper reports that Ferguson was also going to sign highly rated 21-year-old striker <a href="/wiki/Chris_Sutton" title="Chris Sutton">Chris Sutton</a> from Norwich City, but the player headed for Blackburn instead.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/1994%E2%80%9395_Manchester_United_F.C._season" title="1994–95 Manchester United F.C. season">1994–95</a> was a harder season for Ferguson. Cantona assaulted a Crystal Palace supporter in a game at <a href="/wiki/Selhurst_Park" title="Selhurst Park">Selhurst Park</a>, and it seemed likely he would leave English football. An eight-month ban saw Cantona miss the final four months of the season. He also received a 14-day prison sentence for the offence but the sentence was quashed on appeal and replaced by a 120-hour community service order. On the brighter side, United paid a British record fee of £7 million for Newcastle United's prolific striker <a href="/wiki/Andy_Cole" title="Andy Cole">Andy Cole</a>, with young winger <a href="/wiki/Keith_Gillespie" title="Keith Gillespie">Keith Gillespie</a> heading to the north-east in exchange. The season also saw the breakthrough of young players <a href="/wiki/Gary_Neville" title="Gary Neville">Gary Neville</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nicky_Butt" title="Nicky Butt">Nicky Butt</a> and <a href="/wiki/Paul_Scholes" title="Paul Scholes">Paul Scholes</a>, who provided excellent cover for the long periods that United were left without some of their more experienced stars.</p>
<p>However, the championship slipped out of Manchester United's grasp as they drew 1–1 with <a href="/wiki/West_Ham_United_F.C." title="West Ham United F.C.">West Ham United</a> on the final day of the season, when a win would have given them the a third successive league title. United also lost the FA Cup final in a 1–0 defeat by Everton.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1995.E2.80.9398">1995–98</span></h3>
<p>Ferguson was heavily criticised in the summer of 1995 when three of United's star players were allowed to leave and replacements were not bought. First Paul Ince moved to <a href="/wiki/Inter_Milan" title="Inter Milan">Internazionale</a> of Italy for £7.5 million, long-serving striker Mark Hughes was suddenly sold to Chelsea in a £1.5 million deal, and Andrei Kanchelskis was sold to Everton.</p>
<p>Ferguson made an approach for Tottenham winger <a href="/wiki/Darren_Anderton" title="Darren Anderton">Darren Anderton</a>, but the player signed a new contract with the <a href="/wiki/North_London" title="North London">North London</a> club. He then made a bid to sign <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Dutchman</a> <a href="/wiki/Marc_Overmars" title="Marc Overmars">Marc Overmars</a> from <a href="/wiki/AFC_Ajax" title="AFC Ajax">Ajax</a> (the European Cup winners), but the player suffered a serious knee injury and was ruled out for months. Media reports suggested that United were going to make an approach for <a href="/wiki/Juventus_F.C." title="Juventus F.C.">Juventus</a> and Italy forward <a href="/wiki/Roberto_Baggio" title="Roberto Baggio">Roberto Baggio</a>, but the player remained in his homeland and signed for <a href="/wiki/A.C._Milan" title="A.C. Milan">Milan</a> instead.</p>
<p>Ferguson felt that United had a number of young players who were ready to play in the first team. The youngsters, who would be known as "Fergie's Fledglings", included Gary Neville, <a href="/wiki/Phil_Neville" title="Phil Neville">Phil Neville</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Beckham" title="David Beckham">David Beckham</a>, Paul Scholes and Nicky Butt, who would all go on to be important members of the team. And so the <a href="/wiki/1995%E2%80%9396_Manchester_United_F.C._season" title="1995–96 Manchester United F.C. season">1995–96 season</a> began without a major signing, at a time when the likes of Arsenal, Liverpool and Newcastle were making the headlines with big-money signings.</p>
<p>A youthful United team lost 3–1 in their opening league game of the 1995–96 season, against Aston Villa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> On <i><a href="/wiki/Match_of_the_Day" title="Match of the Day">Match of the Day</a></i>, pundit <a href="/wiki/Alan_Hansen" title="Alan Hansen">Alan Hansen</a> criticised their performance, ending his analysis with the words, "You can't win anything with kids."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> United won their next five matches and were boosted by the return of Cantona, who made his comeback against Liverpool in October 1995. For much of the season, the team trailed league leaders Newcastle and found themselves ten points behind by Christmas; this later was narrowed to seven points after defeating them on 27 December 1995. The gap increased to 12 points, but a series of wins, coupled with Newcastle dropping points, meant by late March, United moved to the top of the table. A hard-fought win against Leeds in April prompted Ferguson to accuse his opponents of "cheating" their manager:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>I'm saying to myself these guys have put their manager in trouble and after seeing how they played against us I can only say they're cheating their manager. You think for some of them it's more important to get a result against Manchester United, who are top of the League, than anything else. It's pathetic. No wonder managers get the sack. Of course, when it comes to Newcastle you wait and see the difference. It will be interesting.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>In a televised outburst after his team's win against Leeds, Newcastle manager <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Keegan" title="Kevin Keegan">Kevin Keegan</a> responded angrily to Ferguson's comments: "We're still fighting for this title, and he's got to go to Middlesbrough ... I would love it if we beat them, love it."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> A win against <a href="/wiki/Middlesbrough_F.C." title="Middlesbrough F.C.">Middlesbrough</a> on the final day sealed the title for United and the team beat Liverpool by a goal to nil to win the <a href="/wiki/1996_FA_Cup_Final" title="1996 FA Cup Final">1996 FA Cup Final</a>; this was their second double in three years. A week after the cup final, Ferguson agreed a four-year contract to remain at United.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></p>
<p>United won their fourth league title in five seasons at the end of the <a href="/wiki/1996%E2%80%9397_Manchester_United_F.C._season" title="1996–97 Manchester United F.C. season">1996–97 campaign</a>, made easier by the fact that their rivals were "not up to the job".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> Under Ferguson, the team made a better go in the Champions League and reached the semi-final stage for the first time in 28 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> United did not advance any further, after defeat by <a href="/wiki/Borussia_Dortmund" title="Borussia Dortmund">Borussia Dortmund</a> of Germany.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> Norwegian signings <a href="/wiki/Ole_Gunnar_Solskj%C3%A6r" title="Ole Gunnar Solskjær">Ole Gunnar Solskjær</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ronny_Johnsen" title="Ronny Johnsen">Ronny Johnsen</a> were the notable additions to the squad, with the former ending the season as the club's top goalscorer. In May 1997, Cantona informed Ferguson his decision to retire from football.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-barc_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-barc-84">[84]</a></sup> The player "felt exploited by United's merchandising department" and questioned the ambition of the club, reasons which Ferguson understood.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-barc_84-1"><a href="#cite_note-barc-84">[84]</a></sup> Striker <a href="/wiki/Teddy_Sheringham" title="Teddy Sheringham">Teddy Sheringham</a> was signed as Cantona's replacement from Tottenham Hotspur, with Blackburn defender <a href="/wiki/Henning_Berg" title="Henning Berg">Henning Berg</a> the other significant purchase that summer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> In the close season, United appointed Keane as their new captain. Ferguson described him as "the best all-round player in the game" after the team's <a href="/wiki/1997_FA_Charity_Shield" title="1997 FA Charity Shield">1997 FA Charity Shield</a> win and believed Keane had "all the right ingredients" to succeed from Cantona.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup></p>
<p>Defeat by Leeds United in September 1997 was the team's first league loss in seven months; Keane during the match injured himself and was subsequently ruled out for the rest of the season with ligament damage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> Goalkeeper Peter Schmeichel was placed as captain in his absence. By November, United opened up a four-point lead in the league, which prompted talk of whether any team could catch them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> After Arsenal's defeat of United in the same month, Ferguson acknowledged a one-horse race was "not good for the game" and admitted his opponents "... deserved to win on their second-half performance".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> The fallibilities of Liverpool, Chelsea and Blackburn as league challengers allowed United during the winter to extend their lead by 11 points, albeit with Arsenal having games-in-hand.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> This was enough for Manchester bookmaker <a href="/wiki/Betfred" title="Betfred">Fred Done</a> to pay out on punters who backed the champions retaining their title.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> United in other competitions fared poorly; they went out of the FA Cup in a replay to <a href="/wiki/Barnsley_F.C." title="Barnsley F.C.">Barnsley</a> and were eliminated in the quarter-final stage of the Champions League against <a href="/wiki/AS_Monaco_FC" title="AS Monaco FC">Monaco</a> on away goals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup></p>
<p>Arsenal closed the gap on United in March and a winning goal from their winger Marc Overmars when the two teams met at Old Trafford handed them the initiative.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-overmars_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-overmars-94">[94]</a></sup> Ferguson was bullish of his team's chances despite the setback and insisted that Arsenal "... will find that they start dropping points towards the end of the season – there's no question about that".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-overmars_94-1"><a href="#cite_note-overmars-94">[94]</a></sup> Arsenal however collected maximum points, sealing the title with a win against Everton on 3 May 1998. Ferguson congratulated his opponent <a href="/wiki/Ars%C3%A8ne_Wenger" title="Arsène Wenger">Arsène Wenger</a>, who in his first full season at the club, later completed the double: "I think it's good for my young players to lose on this occasion. I wholeheartedly acknowledge what Arsenal achieved between Christmas and the end of the season."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> United straight after paid £10.75 million for <a href="/wiki/PSV_Eindhoven" title="PSV Eindhoven">PSV</a> defender <a href="/wiki/Jaap_Stam" title="Jaap Stam">Jaap Stam</a>, a new club record fee.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> Ferguson wanted to strengthen the squad's attacking options and identified Aston Villa's <a href="/wiki/Dwight_Yorke" title="Dwight Yorke">Dwight Yorke</a> as his main target.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> Attempts to sign Yorke were rebuffed at first, before Ferguson persuaded Edwards to increase United's initial offer of £10 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-yorke_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-yorke-98">[98]</a></sup> A£12.6 million deal was reached a week into the league campaign; Yorke signed minutes before the deadline to submit United's squad for the Champions League.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-yorke_98-1"><a href="#cite_note-yorke-98">[98]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1998.E2.80.9399:_Treble_success">1998–99: Treble success</span></h3>
<p>United opened the <a href="/wiki/1998%E2%80%9399_Manchester_United_F.C._season" title="1998–99 Manchester United F.C. season">1998–99 season</a> with a 3–0 loss to Arsenal in the <a href="/wiki/1998_FA_Charity_Shield" title="1998 FA Charity Shield">1998 FA Charity Shield</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> The beating did not concern Ferguson, though he described his team's defeat by Arsenal in September 1998 as "a lot less tolerable". In December 1998, Kidd left his role as assistant to become the manager of Blackburn Rovers. Ferguson instructed <a href="/wiki/Eric_Harrison" title="Eric Harrison">Eric Harrison</a> and <a href="/wiki/Les_Kershaw" title="Les Kershaw">Les Kershaw</a> to find suitable replacements, "in terms of coaching ability and work ethic." Both recommended <a href="/wiki/Steve_McClaren" title="Steve McClaren">Steve McClaren</a>, the assistant to <a href="/wiki/Jim_Smith_(footballer,_born_1940)" title="Jim Smith (footballer, born 1940)">Jim Smith</a> at <a href="/wiki/Derby_County_F.C." title="Derby County F.C.">Derby County</a>. McClaren was Ferguson's initial choice and appointed him in February 1999. His first game as assistant was <a href="/wiki/Nottingham_Forest_F.C._1%E2%80%938_Manchester_United_F.C." title="Nottingham Forest F.C. 1–8 Manchester United F.C.">United's 8–1 victory over Nottingham Forest</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup></p>
<p>Ferguson felt United's bid to regain the Premier League began indifferently because of their commitments to other competitions. He was willing to "pay for the progress" made in the Champions League; the team finished second in their Champions League "group of death", behind Bayern Munich and ahead of Barcelona. United's win against Liverpool in the FA Cup fourth round was a portent for the remainder of the season. A goal down after three minutes, the team equalised only until the 86th minute and scored the winning goal through Solskjær in stoppage time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> On reflection, Ferguson said it was "a demonstration of the morale that was to be every bit as vital as rich skill in the five months that lay ahead of United".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mdf_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-mdf-102">[102]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PalmaresManU.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="320" data-file-width="240" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/PalmaresManU.jpg/170px-PalmaresManU.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/ec/PalmaresManU.jpg 1.5x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:PalmaresManU.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Under Ferguson, United acclaimed a treble of trophies in the 1998–99 season.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the final weeks of the league season, Arsenal emerged as a creditable challenger to United. Both clubs were also paired together in the semi-final of the FA Cup, decided by a replay as the original game finished goalless. Keane was sent off in the second half and United conceded a penalty late into the match with the score 1–1. <a href="/wiki/Dennis_Bergkamp" title="Dennis Bergkamp">Dennis Bergkamp</a>'s effort was saved by Peter Schmeichel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-semi_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-semi-103">[103]</a></sup> Ferguson hoped his team "could at least take it to a penalty shoot-out", but instead the match was settled in extra time: Giggs ran the length of the pitch and evaded several Arsenal players to score the winning goal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mdf_102-1"><a href="#cite_note-mdf-102">[102]</a></sup> United went on to beat Newcastle United in the <a href="/wiki/1999_FA_Cup_Final" title="1999 FA Cup Final">1999 FA Cup Final</a> and completed the double – a week earlier the team defeated Tottenham Hotspur to regain the Premier League.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mdf_102-2"><a href="#cite_note-mdf-102">[102]</a></sup></p>
<p>United's progression in the Champions League was promising compared to previous seasons. The team eliminated Inter Milan at the quarter-final stage and faced Juventus in the last four of the competition. A late goal scored by Giggs in the first leg earned the team a 1–1 draw, but in spite of conceding an away goal, Ferguson was adamant of United's chances of reaching the final: "... something tells me we are going to win. The nature of our club is that we torture ourselves so much that the only way to get relief is by winning over there."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/Stadio_delle_Alpi" title="Stadio delle Alpi">Stadio delle Alpi</a>, striker <a href="/wiki/Filippo_Inzaghi" title="Filippo Inzaghi">Filippo Inzaghi</a> scored twice to put Juventus 3–1 up on aggregate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-juv_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-juv-105">[105]</a></sup> Keane headed in a Beckham cross to halve the deficit, but was later shown a yellow card for a foul on <a href="/wiki/Edgar_Davids" title="Edgar Davids">Edgar Davids</a>, which prevented him from playing in the final.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-juv_105-1"><a href="#cite_note-juv-105">[105]</a></sup> Yorke equalised, before Cole added a third to win the match outright.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-juv_105-2"><a href="#cite_note-juv-105">[105]</a></sup> Keane's performance merited praise from Ferguson:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>It was the most emphatic display of selflessness I have seen on a football field. Pounding over every blade of grass, competing if he would rather die of exhaustion than lose, he inspired all around him. I felt it was an honour to be associated with such a player.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mdf_102-3"><a href="#cite_note-mdf-102">[102]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>Days after the FA Cup final, United travelled to Barcelona, the setting for the <a href="/wiki/1999_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="1999 UEFA Champions League Final">1999 UEFA Champions League Final</a>. Ferguson contemplated his team selection against Bayern Munich; suspensions to Scholes and Keane ruled both players out of the match.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mdf_102-4"><a href="#cite_note-mdf-102">[102]</a></sup> Beckham was positioned in centre midfield, while Giggs moved to the right wing and Blomqvist started on the left – changes the manager felt would prevent the opposition from playing narrow.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mdf_102-5"><a href="#cite_note-mdf-102">[102]</a></sup> United conceded in the first six minutes of the final, from a <a href="/wiki/Mario_Basler" title="Mario Basler">Mario Basler</a>'s free kick. Sheringham, who came on for Blomqvist, equalised from a corner in the first minute of additional time. McClaren told Ferguson to get the team organised for extra time, to which he replied, "Steve, this game isn't finished."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mdf_102-6"><a href="#cite_note-mdf-102">[102]</a></sup> Three minutes into added time, Solskjær scored the winner, which for United completed an unprecedented <a href="/wiki/Treble_(association_football)" title="Treble (association football)">treble</a>. Ferguson, interviewed moments after, said, "I can't believe it. I can't believe it. Football, bloody hell. But they never gave in and that's what won it." He and Schmeichel, the stand-in captain, jointly lifted the cup during the trophy presentation.</p>
<p>A crowd of over 500,000 people turned out on the streets of Manchester to greet the players, who paraded through the city in an open-top bus.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> As European champions, United were invited to play in the <a href="/wiki/Intercontinental_Cup_(football)" title="Intercontinental Cup (football)">Intercontinental Cup</a>. The club also entered the inaugural <a href="/wiki/FIFA_Club_World_Cup" title="FIFA Club World Cup">Club World Championship</a>, which was held in Brazil. This brought about a potential <a href="/wiki/Fixture_congestion" title="Fixture congestion">fixture congestion</a> so United accepted the FA's recommendation of withdrawing from the FA Cup, the first holders to do so.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> In later years, Ferguson elaborated on the club's decision: "We did it to help England’s World Cup bid. That was the political situation. I regretted it because we got nothing but stick and terrible criticism for not being in the FA Cup when really, it wasn’t our fault."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1999.E2.80.932002:_Title_hat-trick.2C_retirement_plan">1999–2002: Title hat-trick, retirement plan</span></h3>
<p>Schmeichel's decision to leave United after eight seasons prompted Ferguson to bring in replacements: <a href="/wiki/Mark_Bosnich" title="Mark Bosnich">Mark Bosnich</a> from Aston Villa and Italian <a href="/wiki/Massimo_Taibi" title="Massimo Taibi">Massimo Taibi</a>. The latter featured in four matches, the last of which a 5–0 defeat at Chelsea in October 1999; he was not selected again by Ferguson. United ended the <a href="/wiki/1999%E2%80%932000_Manchester_United_F.C._season" title="1999–2000 Manchester United F.C. season">1999–2000</a> league season as champions, with just three defeats and a record points margin of 18.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> In December 1999, the club beat <a href="/wiki/Sociedade_Esportiva_Palmeiras" title="Sociedade Esportiva Palmeiras">Palmeiras</a> in <a href="/wiki/Tokyo" title="Tokyo">Tokyo</a> to win the Intercontinental Cup,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> but a month later exited at the group stage of the <a href="/wiki/2000_FIFA_Club_World_Championship" title="2000 FIFA Club World Championship">inaugural Club World Championship</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> although Ferguson insisted the tournament was "fantastic".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> United failed to retain the Champions League, as they lost in the quarter-final stage to eventual winners Real Madrid.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> Ferguson sought to strengthen his squad and signed <a href="/wiki/Fabien_Barthez" title="Fabien Barthez">Fabien Barthez</a> from Monaco for £7.8 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> He also monitored the progress of <a href="/wiki/Ruud_van_Nistelrooy" title="Ruud van Nistelrooy">Ruud van Nistelrooy</a>, "a striker of the highest calibre".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-van_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-van-117">[117]</a></sup> He met the player and his agent in Manchester to discuss formalities and was informed of Van Nistelrooy's troubled right knee.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-van_117-1"><a href="#cite_note-van-117">[117]</a></sup> Ferguson was not agitated by this; he recalled from experience a similar niggle that did not stop his playing career.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-van_117-2"><a href="#cite_note-van-117">[117]</a></sup> Van Nistelrooy, however, failed his medical, but Ferguson reassured him that "we might yet find a way out of the nightmare".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-van_117-3"><a href="#cite_note-van-117">[117]</a></sup> The deal was resurrected in April 2001 for a British record transfer fee of £19 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/2000%E2%80%9301_Manchester_United_F.C._season" title="2000–01 Manchester United F.C. season">2000–01 season</a>, United retained the league title for a third season, becoming only the fourth side in history to do so. The achievement was overshadowed by reports of a rift between the club's board and Ferguson.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> He told the club's television channel <a href="/wiki/MUTV_(Manchester_United_F.C.)" title="MUTV (Manchester United F.C.)">MUTV</a> that he was prepared to sever all ties with the club, once his contract ended the following year: "The decision has been taken. I'm going to leave the club. I'm disappointed with what has happened because I was hoping something would be sorted out. It hasn't happened as I thought it would and that's all there is to it."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> Both parties eventually reached a compromise which pleased Ferguson: "I am delighted we've settled this. When you have been at the club as long as I have it gets in your blood."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> Ferguson's decision to retire came about because he perceived his chances of winning a second European Cup as "imponderable." Age was another factor: reaching 60 acted as a "psychological barrier ... It changed my sense of my own fitness, my health."</p>
<p>In May 2001, McClaren left to become Middlesbrough manager,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> with <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Ryan_(footballer,_born_1945)" title="Jimmy Ryan (footballer, born 1945)">Jimmy Ryan</a> being named assistant to Ferguson for the duration of the campaign.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> United once more broke their transfer record with the purchase of <a href="/wiki/Juan_Sebasti%C3%A1n_Ver%C3%B3n" title="Juan Sebastián Verón">Juan Sebastián Verón</a> from <a href="/wiki/S.S._Lazio" title="S.S. Lazio">Lazio</a> for a reported £28.1 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> In August 2001, Stam was transferred to Lazio for £16 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> The player reportedly moved because of claims in his autobiography <i>Head to Head</i>; Stam implied that Ferguson illegally contacted him about a move to Manchester United, before informing PSV.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stam_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-stam-126">[126]</a></sup> Ferguson said he sold the player because the club needed to cut back on its "massive wage bill".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-blanc_127-0"><a href="#cite_note-blanc-127">[127]</a></sup> He replaced the defender with <a href="/wiki/Laurent_Blanc" title="Laurent Blanc">Laurent Blanc</a>, a long sought-after target.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-blanc_127-1"><a href="#cite_note-blanc-127">[127]</a></sup> In an interview with <a href="/wiki/Alastair_Campbell" title="Alastair Campbell">Alastair Campbell</a> eight years after, Ferguson described his biggest mistake at the club was "letting go of Jaap Stam. No question".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup></p>
<p>The club endured a poor first half to the season and languished in ninth position after a home defeat by West Ham in December 2001.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> On the night of Christmas Day, Ferguson shelved his retirement plan. His family convinced him to remain in charge of United; Cathy bluntly listed her reasoning: "One, your health is good. Two, I'm not having you in the house. And three, you're too young anyway." Ferguson informed Watkins of his u-turn the following day and resumed work at once.</p>
<p>Once Ferguson publicised his decision to remain in February 2002, United's form improved. The team won 13 out of 15 matches, though finished third in the league behind Arsenal and Liverpool. United was unsuccessful in Europe, losing their Champions League semi-final on away goals to <a href="/wiki/Bayer_04_Leverkusen" title="Bayer 04 Leverkusen">Bayer Leverkusen</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> Early exits from the League Cup and FA Cup meant they ended the season trophyless. Ferguson himself admitted that the decision to pre-announce his retirement had resulted in a negative effect on the players and on his ability to impose discipline.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2002.E2.80.932006:_Rebuilding_and_transition">2002–2006: Rebuilding and transition</span></h3>
<p>In June 2002, Ferguson appointed <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Queiroz" title="Carlos Queiroz">Carlos Queiroz</a> as his new assistant.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> The recommendation came from <a href="/wiki/Andy_Roxburgh" title="Andy Roxburgh">Andy Roxburgh</a>, at a time when United began scouting for southern-hemisphere footballers and wanted a multilingual coach. Ferguson was so impressed with Queiroz after their first meeting, he offered him the job "right away". In July 2002, United paid £29.3 million for Leeds United defender <a href="/wiki/Rio_Ferdinand" title="Rio Ferdinand">Rio Ferdinand</a>. The club broke the British transfer record once more, though this did not concern Ferguson: "We have the right to try and improve ourselves and there's nothing wrong with that."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:C_ronaldo_cropped.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="691" data-file-width="402" height="292" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/C_ronaldo_cropped.png/170px-C_ronaldo_cropped.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/C_ronaldo_cropped.png/255px-C_ronaldo_cropped.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/C_ronaldo_cropped.png/340px-C_ronaldo_cropped.png 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:C_ronaldo_cropped.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
United signed <a href="/wiki/Cristiano_Ronaldo" title="Cristiano Ronaldo">Cristiano Ronaldo</a> in August 2003.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/2002%E2%80%9303_Manchester_United_F.C._season" title="2002–03 Manchester United F.C. season">2002–03 season</a> began rather poorly for United; the club made its worst start to a league campaign in 13 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> In a column for <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Telegraph" title="The Daily Telegraph">The Daily Telegraph</a></i>, Hansen said Ferguson "will recognise this difficult start to the season for what it is: the greatest challenge of his career".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> Ferguson's response was typically bullish:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>I don't get paid to panic. We have had plenty of stuttering starts. My greatest challenge is not what's happening at the moment. My greatest challenge was knocking Liverpool right off their fucking perch. And you can print that.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>Several players were sent away for surgery in this period, a "minor gamble" Ferguson took in the hope they would return energised. Defeats, such as the one to Manchester City at Maine Road in November 2002, forced United to change their playing style. The team "moved the ball forward more and quicker rather than concentrating on possession ratios," and the coaching staff tried accommodating <a href="/wiki/Diego_Forl%C3%A1n" title="Diego Forlán">Diego Forlán</a> with Ruud van Nistelrooy, before settling with Paul Scholes. United's league form improved as the season went on despite defeat by Liverpool in the <a href="/wiki/2003_Football_League_Cup_Final" title="2003 Football League Cup Final">2003 Football League Cup Final</a> and they overhauled Arsenal to win the Premier League for an eighth time in May 2003.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> The team was eliminated in the Champions League quarter-final to Real Madrid over two legs; Ferguson described the second match, a 4–3 win at Old Trafford as "epic".</p>
<p>After a season at United, Queiroz left to manage Real Madrid in June 2003.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> Ferguson anticipated his deputy would return – "Three months later, he was wanting to quit Madrid," and for that reason did not appoint a replacement. In the summer, David Beckham also moved to Real Madrid, while Juan Sebastián Verón joined Chelsea. United in the meantime rebuilt their team: <a href="/wiki/Tim_Howard" title="Tim Howard">Tim Howard</a> replaced Barthez in goal and <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Kl%C3%A9berson" title="José Kléberson">Kléberson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eric_Djemba-Djemba" title="Eric Djemba-Djemba">Eric Djemba-Djemba</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cristiano_Ronaldo" title="Cristiano Ronaldo">Cristiano Ronaldo</a> came in to bolster the squad. <a href="/wiki/Ronaldinho" title="Ronaldinho">Ronaldinho</a> might have also joined "had he not said yes, then no, to our offer". Ferguson admitted the signings the club made did not work out in hindsight: "We rushed down the path of buying in proven players – who we thought would match our standards right away."</p>
