<p>In December 2003, Rio Ferdinand was banned from playing football for eight months after he failed to present himself at a drugs test.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> Ferguson in his autobiography ten years later blamed the drug testers, who "...didn't do their job. They didn't go looking for Rio". The absence of Ferdinand hampered United's defence of the Premier League in the <a href="/wiki/2003%E2%80%9304_Manchester_United_F.C._season" title="2003–04 Manchester United F.C. season">2003–04 season</a>; the team finished third behind Arsenal's "<a href="/wiki/The_Invincibles_(football)" title="The Invincibles (football)">Invincibles</a>" and Chelsea. In Europe, they experienced defeat at the hands of eventual winners <a href="/wiki/FC_Porto" title="FC Porto">Porto</a>. Ferguson felt it was possible "not because of the performance of the players but because of the referee", who disallowed a legitimate Scholes goal that would have been enough to progress. United ended the campaign as FA Cup winners, beating <a href="/wiki/Millwall_F.C." title="Millwall F.C.">Millwall</a> 3–0 in the <a href="/wiki/2004_FA_Cup_Final" title="2004 FA Cup Final">2004 final</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup></p>
<p>At the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/2004%E2%80%9305_Manchester_United_F.C._season" title="2004–05 Manchester United F.C. season">2004–05 season</a>, teenage striker <a href="/wiki/Wayne_Rooney" title="Wayne Rooney">Wayne Rooney</a> (the world's most expensive teenager at more than £20 million) and Argentine defender <a href="/wiki/Gabriel_Heinze" title="Gabriel Heinze">Gabriel Heinze</a> joined United while Cristiano Ronaldo continued where he had left off the previous season by putting in more match-winning performances. But the lack of a striker after Ruud van Nistelrooy spent most of the season injured saw the club finish third for the third time in four seasons. In the <a href="/wiki/2004%E2%80%9305_FA_Cup" title="2004–05 FA Cup">2004–05 FA Cup</a>, they lost on <a href="/wiki/Penalty_shoot-out_(association_football)" title="Penalty shoot-out (association football)">penalties</a> to Arsenal. A second round exit from the European Cup at the hands of Milan and a semi-final exit from the League Cup at the hands of eventual winners Chelsea (who also clinched the Premier League title) meant that 2004–05 was a rare instance of a trophyless season for United. During the season, Ferguson managed his 1,000th game in charge of United in a 2–1 home win against <a href="/wiki/Olympique_Lyonnais" title="Olympique Lyonnais">Lyon</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup></p>
<p>Ferguson's preparations for the <a href="/wiki/2005%E2%80%9306_Manchester_United_F.C._season" title="2005–06 Manchester United F.C. season">2005–06 season</a> were disrupted by a high-profile dispute with major shareholder <a href="/wiki/John_Magnier" title="John Magnier">John Magnier</a>, over the ownership of the racehorse <a href="/wiki/Rock_of_Gibraltar_(horse)" title="Rock of Gibraltar (horse)">Rock of Gibraltar</a>. When Magnier and business partner <a href="/wiki/J._P._McManus" title="J. P. McManus">J. P. McManus</a> agreed to sell their shares to American business tycoon <a href="/wiki/Malcolm_Glazer" title="Malcolm Glazer">Malcolm Glazer</a>, it cleared the way for Glazer to acquire full control of the club. This sparked violent protests from United fans,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> and disrupted Ferguson's plans to strengthen the team in the transfer market. In spite of this, United looked to solve their goalkeeping and midfield problems. For this, they signed the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_national_football_team" title="Netherlands national football team">Dutch</a> goalkeeper <a href="/wiki/Edwin_van_der_Sar" title="Edwin van der Sar">Edwin van der Sar</a> from <a href="/wiki/Fulham_F.C." title="Fulham F.C.">Fulham</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_Korea_national_football_team" title="South Korea national football team">Korean</a> star <a href="/wiki/Park_Ji-sung" title="Park Ji-sung">Park Ji-sung</a> from PSV.</p>
<p>The season was one of transition. On 18 November, Roy Keane officially left the club, his contract ended by mutual consent. United failed to qualify for the knock-out phase of the UEFA Champions' League. In the January transfer window, Serbian defender <a href="/wiki/Nemanja_Vidi%C4%87" title="Nemanja Vidić">Nemanja Vidić</a> and French full-back <a href="/wiki/Patrice_Evra" title="Patrice Evra">Patrice Evra</a> were signed, and the side finished in second place in the league, behind runaway leaders Chelsea. Winning the League Cup was a consolation prize for lack of success elsewhere. Ruud van Nistelrooy's future at Old Trafford seemed to be in doubt after not starting in the League Cup final, and he departed at the end of the season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup></p>
<p>Before the start of the new season, Ferguson received much criticism, particular in the guise of an article in <i>The Guardian</i> titled "Shredding his legacy at every turn".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Second_European_Champions_League">Second European Champions League</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ferguson_and_Queiroz.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="580" data-file-width="324" height="304" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Ferguson_and_Queiroz.jpg/170px-Ferguson_and_Queiroz.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Ferguson_and_Queiroz.jpg/255px-Ferguson_and_Queiroz.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/ab/Ferguson_and_Queiroz.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ferguson_and_Queiroz.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Ferguson with former assistant manager <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Queiroz" title="Carlos Queiroz">Carlos Queiroz</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 2006, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Carrick" title="Michael Carrick">Michael Carrick</a> was signed to take Roy Keane's place in the team for a fee that eventually rose to £18 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Taylor_146-0"><a href="#cite_note-Taylor-146">[146]</a></sup> United started the season well, and for the first time ever won their first four Premier League games, United's best start since 1985.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Taylor_146-1"><a href="#cite_note-Taylor-146">[146]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup> They set the early pace in the Premier League and never relinquished top spot from the tenth match of the 38-game season. The January 2006 signings had a huge impact on United's performances – Patrice Evra and Nemanja Vidić came in to form a solid back line along with already existing players Rio Ferdinand and skipper Gary Neville. The signing of Carrick, which was questioned and criticised by a large portion of the media, brought stability and further creativity in the United midfield, forming an effective partnership with Paul Scholes. Park Ji-sung and Ryan Giggs both underlined their value to the first team squad by adding significant pace and incisiveness in attack with Wayne Rooney and Cristiano Ronaldo.</p>
<p>Ferguson celebrated the 20th anniversary of his appointment as manager of Manchester United on 6 November 2006. Tributes also came from Ferguson's players, both past and present,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Robbins_148-0"><a href="#cite_note-Robbins-148">[148]</a></sup> as well as his old foe, Arsène Wenger,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wenger_149-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wenger-149">[149]</a></sup> his old captain, Roy Keane, and current players. The party was spoiled the following day when United endured a single-goal defeat at the hands of <a href="/wiki/Southend_United_F.C." title="Southend United F.C.">Southend United</a> in the fourth round of the League Cup.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup> On 1 December, however, it was announced that Manchester United had signed 35-year-old <a href="/wiki/Henrik_Larsson" title="Henrik Larsson">Henrik Larsson</a> on loan,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Larsson_151-0"><a href="#cite_note-Larsson-151">[151]</a></sup> a player that Ferguson had admired for many years, and attempted to capture previously. On 23 December 2006, Cristiano Ronaldo scored the club's 2,000th goal under the helm of Ferguson in a match against Aston Villa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup></p>
<p>Manchester United subsequently won their ninth Premier League title but were denied a unique fourth double by Chelsea's <a href="/wiki/Didier_Drogba" title="Didier Drogba">Didier Drogba</a> scoring a late goal in the FA Cup final at <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium" title="Wembley Stadium">Wembley Stadium</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup> In the Champions League, the club reached the semi-finals, recording a 7–1 home win over <a href="/wiki/A.S._Roma" title="A.S. Roma">Roma</a> in the quarter-final second leg,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup> but lost at the <a href="/wiki/San_Siro" title="San Siro">San Siro</a> to Milan 3–0 in the second leg of the semi-final after being 3–2 up from the first leg.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup></p>
<p>For the <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%9308_Manchester_United_F.C._season" title="2007–08 Manchester United F.C. season">2007–08 season</a>, Ferguson made notable signings to reinforce United's first team. Long-term target <a href="/wiki/Owen_Hargreaves" title="Owen Hargreaves">Owen Hargreaves</a> joined from Bayern Munich, young Portuguese winger <a href="/wiki/Nani" title="Nani">Nani</a> and Brazilian playmaker <a href="/wiki/Anderson_(footballer,_born_1988)" title="Anderson (footballer, born 1988)">Anderson</a> joined soon after, while the last summer signing was West Ham and <a href="/wiki/Argentina_national_football_team" title="Argentina national football team">Argentina</a> striker <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Tevez" title="Carlos Tevez">Carlos Tevez</a> after a complex and protracted transfer saga.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup></p>
<p>United suffered their worst start to a season under Ferguson, drawing their first two league games before suffering a 1–0 defeat by local rivals Manchester City.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup> United, however, recovered and began a tight race with Arsenal for the title. After a good run of form, Ferguson claimed that throughout his time at Manchester United, this was the best squad he had managed to assemble thus far.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BestSquad_161-0"><a href="#cite_note-BestSquad-161">[161]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 16 February 2008, United beat Arsenal 4–0 in an FA Cup Fifth Round match at Old Trafford,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup> but were knocked out by eventual winners <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_F.C." title="Portsmouth F.C.">Portsmouth</a> in the quarter-final on 8 March, losing 1–0 at home.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup> United having had a penalty claim turned down, Ferguson alleged after the game that <a href="/wiki/Keith_Hackett" title="Keith Hackett">Keith Hackett</a>, general manager of the <a href="/wiki/Professional_Game_Match_Officials_Board" title="Professional Game Match Officials Board">Professional Game Match Officials Board</a>, was "not doing his job properly".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup> Ferguson was subsequently charged by <a href="/wiki/The_Football_Association" title="The Football Association">The FA</a> with improper conduct, which he decided to contest. This was the second charge Ferguson faced in the season, following his complaints against the referee after United lost 1–0 at <a href="/wiki/Bolton_Wanderers_F.C." title="Bolton Wanderers F.C.">Bolton Wanderers</a> – a charge he decided not to contest.</p>
<p>On 11 May 2008, Ferguson led Manchester United to a tenth Premier League title, exactly 25 years to the day after he led Aberdeen to European glory against Real Madrid in the European Cup Winners' Cup. Nearest rivals Chelsea – level on points going into the final round of matches, but with an inferior goal difference – could only draw 1–1 at home to Bolton, finishing two points adrift of the champions. United's title win was sealed with a 2–0 win over <a href="/wiki/Wigan_Athletic_F.C." title="Wigan Athletic F.C.">Wigan Athletic</a>, managed by former United captain Steve Bruce.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SAF_CL_semi_2009.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3057" data-file-width="2035" height="255" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/SAF_CL_semi_2009.jpg/170px-SAF_CL_semi_2009.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/SAF_CL_semi_2009.jpg/255px-SAF_CL_semi_2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/SAF_CL_semi_2009.jpg/340px-SAF_CL_semi_2009.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:SAF_CL_semi_2009.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Ferguson in 2009</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 21 May 2008, Ferguson won his second European Cup with Manchester United as they beat Chelsea 6–5 on penalties in the <a href="/wiki/Luzhniki_Stadium" title="Luzhniki Stadium">Luzhniki Stadium</a> in <a href="/wiki/Moscow" title="Moscow">Moscow</a>, following a 1–1 draw after extra time in the first ever all-English UEFA Champions League Final.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup> A penalty miss from Cristiano Ronaldo meant that <a href="/wiki/John_Terry" title="John Terry">John Terry</a>'s spot-kick would have given the trophy to Chelsea if successfully converted, but Terry blew his chance of glory and in the end it was Edwin van der Sar's blocking of a <a href="/wiki/Nicolas_Anelka" title="Nicolas Anelka">Nicolas Anelka</a> penalty which gave the trophy to Manchester United for the second time under Ferguson and for the third time overall.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Another_two_league_titles_and_League_Cups">Another two league titles and League Cups</span></h3>
<p>Although the team had a slow start to the <a href="/wiki/2008%E2%80%9309_Manchester_United_F.C._season" title="2008–09 Manchester United F.C. season">2008–09 season</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup> United won the Premier League with a game to spare,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup> making Ferguson the first manager in the history of English football to win the Premier League three times consecutively, on two separate occasions. Ferguson had now won 11 league titles at Manchester United, and the 2008–09 season title success put them level with Liverpool as league champions on a record 18 occasions in total.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup> They also won the League Cup on penalties after a goalless Wembley draw with Tottenham.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup></p>
<p>They contested the <a href="/wiki/2009_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="2009 UEFA Champions League Final">2009 Champions League final</a> against Barcelona on 27 May 2009 but lost 2–0.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup></p>
<p>After the presentation ceremony, Ferguson conceded that he would stay on at United for as long as his health permitted him and that he would be glad to win the league title once more. This would make United's total league wins one more than rivals Liverpool, becoming the outright leader in total wins.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup></p>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_Manchester_United_F.C._season" title="2009–10 Manchester United F.C. season">2009–10</a>, Ferguson added another League Cup to his honours list as United defeated Aston Villa 2–1 in the Wembley final on 28 February 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup> However, his dreams of a third European Cup were ended a few weeks later when United were edged out of the competition in the quarter-finals by Bayern Munich on away goals. And their hopes of a record 19th league title were ended on the last day of the season when Chelsea beat them to the Premier League title, crushing Wigan Athletic 8–0 and rendering United's 4–0 win over <a href="/wiki/Stoke_City_F.C." title="Stoke City F.C.">Stoke City</a> meaningless.</p>
<p>On 8 August 2010, Ferguson added another <a href="/wiki/FA_Community_Shield" title="FA Community Shield">FA Community Shield</a> to his honours list as United defeated Chelsea 3–1 in the final in Wembley. On 19 December 2010, Ferguson became Manchester United's longest serving manager in history, overtaking Matt Busby's record of 24 years, 1 month and 13 days in charge of the club.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup> He ended the season by winning his 12th and Manchester United's 19th league title and thus overtaking Liverpool's record of 18. Manchester United faced Barcelona again on 28 May 2011 in the <a href="/wiki/2011_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="2011 UEFA Champions League Final">2011 Champions League final</a>, their third in four years, but United lost 3–1. Analyst Alan Hansen stated that he believed Ferguson was "the key component" in United's success that season, so key in fact that "[he] would have claimed the crown with any of the other top sides had he been in charge of them".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup> With Edwin van der Sar, Gary Neville and Paul Scholes all retiring in 2011,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup> Ferguson spent big by signing defender <a href="/wiki/Phil_Jones_(footballer,_born_1992)" title="Phil Jones (footballer, born 1992)">Phil Jones</a> from Blackburn and winger <a href="/wiki/Ashley_Young" title="Ashley Young">Ashley Young</a> from Aston Villa for around £17 million each,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup> and goalkeeper <a href="/wiki/David_de_Gea" title="David de Gea">David de Gea</a> from <a href="/wiki/Atl%C3%A9tico_Madrid" title="Atlético Madrid">Atlético Madrid</a> for around £19 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 2 September 2012, Ferguson managed his 1,000th league game with United against <a href="/wiki/Southampton_F.C." title="Southampton F.C.">Southampton</a>. United won the game 3–2 thanks to a hat-trick from <a href="/wiki/Robin_van_Persie" title="Robin van Persie">Robin van Persie</a>. Two weeks later, he won his 100th game in the Champions League with a 1–0 win over <a href="/wiki/Galatasaray_S.K._(football)" title="Galatasaray S.K. (football)">Galatasaray</a> at Old Trafford.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Retirement">Retirement</span></h3>
<p>On 8 May 2013, Ferguson announced that he was to retire as manager at the end of the football season, but would remain at the club as a director and club ambassador.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-retirement_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-retirement-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup> <i>The Guardian</i> announced it was the "end of an era",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup> while <a href="/wiki/UEFA" title="UEFA">UEFA</a> president <a href="/wiki/Michel_Platini" title="Michel Platini">Michel Platini</a> said that Ferguson was "a true visionary".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Prime Minister of the United Kingdom">Prime Minister of the United Kingdom</a> <a href="/wiki/David_Cameron" title="David Cameron">David Cameron</a> described Ferguson as a "remarkable man in British football".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189"><a href="#cite_note-189">[189]</a></sup> Former Manchester United players Paul Ince and Bryan Robson agreed that Ferguson would be "a hard act to follow".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190"><a href="#cite_note-190">[190]</a></sup> Manchester United co-chairman <a href="/wiki/Joel_Glazer" title="Joel Glazer">Joel Glazer</a> said, "His determination to succeed and dedication to the club have been truly remarkable."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191"><a href="#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup> Ferguson revealed that he had in fact decided that he was going to retire back in December 2012 and that it had been very difficult not to reveal his plans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192"><a href="#cite_note-192">[192]</a></sup> Ferguson's decision to retire saw United shares fall 5% on the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Stock_Exchange" title="New York Stock Exchange">New York Stock Exchange</a>. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193"><a href="#cite_note-193">[193]</a></sup> <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194"><a href="#cite_note-194">[194]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 9 May 2013, Manchester United announced Everton manager <a href="/wiki/David_Moyes" title="David Moyes">David Moyes</a> would replace Ferguson as the club manager from 1 July, having signed a six-year contract.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195"><a href="#cite_note-195">[195]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196"><a href="#cite_note-196">[196]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197"><a href="#cite_note-197">[197]</a></sup> Ryan Giggs, however, took over as interim player-manager ten months later, on 22 April 2014, when Moyes was sacked after a poor season in which the club failed to defend their Premier League title and failed to qualify for the Champions League for the first time since 1995–96.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198"><a href="#cite_note-198">[198]</a></sup></p>
<p>Ferguson released his second autobiography in October 2013 called <i><a href="/wiki/Alex_Ferguson:_My_Autobiography" title="Alex Ferguson: My Autobiography">My Autobiography</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199"><a href="#cite_note-199">[199]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-200"><a href="#cite_note-200">[200]</a></sup></p>
<p>In January, 2014, Ferguson was appointed as the UEFA Coaching Ambassador,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201"><a href="#cite_note-201">[201]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202"><a href="#cite_note-202">[202]</a></sup> and said it was "an honour and a privilege" to be given the role.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203"><a href="#cite_note-203">[203]</a></sup> In April 2014, it was announced that Ferguson would be taking up a "long-term teaching position" at <a href="/wiki/Harvard_University" title="Harvard University">Harvard University</a>, where he would be lecturing on a new course titled "The Business of Entertainment, Media and Sports".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204"><a href="#cite_note-204">[204]</a></sup> This came six months after he revealed his blueprint for success was included in the <i><a href="/wiki/Harvard_Business_Review" title="Harvard Business Review">Harvard Business Review</a></i> in a series of interviews with <a href="/wiki/Anita_Elberse" title="Anita Elberse">Anita Elberse</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-205"><a href="#cite_note-205">[205]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-206"><a href="#cite_note-206">[206]</a></sup> His third book, <i>Leadership</i>, was published in collaboration with <a href="/wiki/Michael_Moritz" title="Michael Moritz">Michael Moritz</a> in August 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-207"><a href="#cite_note-207">[207]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Controversies">Controversies</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Gordon_Strachan">Gordon Strachan</span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Gordon_Strachan" title="Gordon Strachan">Gordon Strachan</a> was a key player for Ferguson at Aberdeen, but their relationship broke down when Strachan signed an agreement with German club <a href="/wiki/1._FC_K%C3%B6ln" title="1. FC Köln">1. FC Köln</a> without telling Ferguson.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fergie_v_Strachan_208-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fergie_v_Strachan-208">[208]</a></sup> Ferguson said that he believed although "there was a cunning streak in Strachan, I had never imagined that he could pull such a stroke on me".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fergie_v_Strachan_208-1"><a href="#cite_note-Fergie_v_Strachan-208">[208]</a></sup> Strachan did not sign for Köln, but instead moved to Manchester United in the summer of 1984.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fergie_v_Strachan_208-2"><a href="#cite_note-Fergie_v_Strachan-208">[208]</a></sup> Strachan liked the move because he felt that Ron Atkinson treated him as an adult, unlike Ferguson.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-209"><a href="#cite_note-209">[209]</a></sup> Strachan was still with the club when Ferguson was appointed manager in November 1986.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fergie_v_Strachan_208-3"><a href="#cite_note-Fergie_v_Strachan-208">[208]</a></sup> Ferguson thought that Strachan did not play for United with the same confidence he had in Scotland and subsequently sold him to Leeds United in 1989.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fergie_v_Strachan_208-4"><a href="#cite_note-Fergie_v_Strachan-208">[208]</a></sup> Strachan enjoyed significant success with Leeds as a veteran player, helping them win the <a href="/wiki/1991%E2%80%9392_in_English_football" title="1991–92 in English football">1991–92</a> English league championship in a title race with Ferguson's United.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fergie_v_Strachan_208-5"><a href="#cite_note-Fergie_v_Strachan-208">[208]</a></sup></p>
<p>Their relationship continued to be frosty as Strachan moved into management himself.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fergie_v_Strachan_208-6"><a href="#cite_note-Fergie_v_Strachan-208">[208]</a></sup> In his 1999 autobiography, Ferguson stated that Strachan "could not be trusted an inch – I would not want to expose my back to him in a hurry".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fergie_v_Strachan_208-7"><a href="#cite_note-Fergie_v_Strachan-208">[208]</a></sup> Strachan's reaction to the attack, in his own autobiography, <i>My Life in Football</i>, was one of being "surprised and disappointed", although he suspected that Ferguson had helped to relegate Strachan's <a href="/wiki/Coventry_City_F.C." title="Coventry City F.C.">Coventry City</a> in 2001 by fielding a weakened Manchester United team in a match against Derby County.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fergie_v_Strachan_208-8"><a href="#cite_note-Fergie_v_Strachan-208">[208]</a></sup> By 2006 they appeared to have "declared something of a truce",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fergie_v_Strachan_208-9"><a href="#cite_note-Fergie_v_Strachan-208">[208]</a></sup> ahead of Champions League matches between United and Strachan's Celtic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-210"><a href="#cite_note-210">[210]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="David_Beckham">David Beckham</span></h3>
<p>In 2003, Ferguson was involved in a dressing room argument with United player David Beckham.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-factfilemmedia_211-0"><a href="#cite_note-factfilemmedia-211">[211]</a></sup> Ferguson allegedly kicked a football boot in frustration, which hit the player in the face and caused a minor injury to Beckham.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Champions_League_draw_fixing">Champions League draw fixing</span></h3>
<p>On 5 April 2003, Ferguson claimed that the Champions League draw was fixed in favour of Spanish and Italian teams.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-factfilemmedia_211-1"><a href="#cite_note-factfilemmedia-211">[211]</a></sup> UEFA charged Ferguson for bringing the game into disrepute with his comments, and on 1 May that year he was fined 10,000 Swiss francs (£4,600).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rock_of_Gibraltar">Rock of Gibraltar</span></h3>
<p>In 2003, Ferguson launched legal action against the then major United shareholder <a href="/wiki/John_Magnier" title="John Magnier">John Magnier</a> over stud rights for race horse <a href="/wiki/Rock_of_Gibraltar_(horse)" title="Rock of Gibraltar (horse)">Rock of Gibraltar</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-212"><a href="#cite_note-212">[212]</a></sup> Magnier counter-sued Ferguson<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-213"><a href="#cite_note-213">[213]</a></sup> by filing a "Motion to Comply" requiring Ferguson to substantiate his claim for half of Rock of Gibraltar's stud fees. The legal issues were further compounded by the request for "99 Questions" to be answered over Ferguson's transfer dealings, including those of Jaap Stam, Juan Sebastián Verón, Tim Howard, <a href="/wiki/David_Bellion" title="David Bellion">David Bellion</a>, Cristiano Ronaldo and Kléberson.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-214"><a href="#cite_note-214">[214]</a></sup> The case was eventually settled out of Court.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_BBC">The BBC</span></h3>
<p>Ferguson refused to give interviews to the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> after a documentary called <i>Fergie and Son</i> was shown on <a href="/wiki/BBC_Three" title="BBC Three">BBC Three</a> on 27 May 2004.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-215"><a href="#cite_note-215">[215]</a></sup> According to an article in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Independent" title="The Independent">The Independent</a></i> newspaper, the documentary had "portrayed his agent son, Jason, as somebody who exploited his father's influence and position to his own ends in the transfer market". The same newspaper article made it clear that "Ferguson Jnr" was never found guilty of any wrongdoing, and it quoted Ferguson Senior as follows: "They [the BBC] did a story about my son that was whole lot of nonsense. It all  [<i><a href="/wiki/Sic" title="Sic">sic</a></i>] made-up stuff and 'brown paper bags' and all that kind of carry-on. It was a horrible attack on my son's honour and he should never have been accused of that."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-216"><a href="#cite_note-216">[216]</a></sup> Subsequent interviews on BBC programmes such as <i><a href="/wiki/Match_of_the_Day" title="Match of the Day">Match of the Day</a></i> were done by his assistant Carlos Queiroz, and later <a href="/wiki/Mike_Phelan" title="Mike Phelan">Mike Phelan</a>.</p>
<p>Under new Premiership rules intended for the 2010–11 season, Ferguson was required to end his BBC boycott.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-217"><a href="#cite_note-217">[217]</a></sup> However, he refused to end his boycott and Manchester United confirmed the club would pay the resulting fines.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-218"><a href="#cite_note-218">[218]</a></sup> On 25 August 2011, Ferguson met with BBC director general <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mark_Thompson_(television_executive)" title="Mark Thompson (television executive)">Mark Thompson</a> and BBC North director <a href="/wiki/Peter_Salmon_(producer)" title="Peter Salmon (producer)">Peter Salmon</a>; the result of the meeting was that Ferguson agreed to end his seven-year boycott.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Recalling_of_loan_players">Recalling of loan players</span></h3>
<p>Following the sacking of his son <a href="/wiki/Darren_Ferguson" title="Darren Ferguson">Darren</a> by <a href="/wiki/Preston_North_End_F.C." title="Preston North End F.C.">Preston North End</a>, Ferguson immediately recalled loaned players <a href="/wiki/Ritchie_De_Laet" title="Ritchie De Laet">Ritchie De Laet</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joshua_King_(footballer)" title="Joshua King (footballer)">Joshua King</a> and <a href="/wiki/Matty_James" title="Matty James">Matty James</a> from Preston under its new managerial system. He later explained that it was the players' own request not to return to Preston after the change of manager.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-219"><a href="#cite_note-219">[219]</a></sup> Stoke City manager <a href="/wiki/Tony_Pulis" title="Tony Pulis">Tony Pulis</a> followed soon after in recalling two former Manchester United players from Preston as well, stating the need for the players to supplement his team's intensive schedule.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-220"><a href="#cite_note-220">[220]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Referees">Referees</span></h3>
<p>Ferguson has received numerous punishments for abusing and publicly criticising match officials when he has perceived them to be at fault:</p>
<ul>
<li>20 October 2003 – Two match touchline ban and fined £10,000 after using abusive and/or insulting words towards fourth official <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Winter" title="Jeff Winter">Jeff Winter</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-221"><a href="#cite_note-221">[221]</a></sup></li>
<li>14 December 2007 – Two match touchline ban and fined £5,000 after using abusive and/or insulting words towards <a href="/wiki/Mark_Clattenburg" title="Mark Clattenburg">Mark Clattenburg</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-222"><a href="#cite_note-222">[222]</a></sup></li>
<li>18 November 2008 – Two match touchline ban and fined £10,000 after confronting <a href="/wiki/Mike_Dean_(referee)" title="Mike Dean (referee)">Mike Dean</a> after a game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-223"><a href="#cite_note-223">[223]</a></sup></li>
<li>12 November 2009 – Four match touchline ban (two suspended) and fined £20,000 for comments made about the fitness of <a href="/wiki/Alan_Wiley" title="Alan Wiley">Alan Wiley</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-224"><a href="#cite_note-224">[224]</a></sup></li>
<li>16 March 2011 – Five match touchline ban (three plus the two suspended for the above offence) and fined £30,000 for comments made questioning the performance and fairness of <a href="/wiki/Martin_Atkinson" title="Martin Atkinson">Martin Atkinson</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-225"><a href="#cite_note-225">[225]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<p>It has also been suggested that Ferguson's intimidation of referees results in so-called "Fergie Time": that is, unusually generous <a href="/wiki/Association_football#Duration_and_tie-breaking_methods" title="Association football">injury time</a> being added in matches where Manchester United are behind. The phrase is at least as old as 2004,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-226"><a href="#cite_note-226">[226]</a></sup> and a statistical analysis by <i><a href="/wiki/The_Times" title="The Times">The Times</a></i> suggests that this comment might be valid, though the article points out that other footballing criteria may explain the correlation between extra added time and United being behind.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-227"><a href="#cite_note-227">[227]</a></sup> Analysis by <a href="/wiki/Opta_Sports" title="Opta Sports">Opta Sports</a> of Premier League matches played between 2010 and 2012 found on average that 79 seconds more time was played in matches where Manchester United were losing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fergie_time_228-0"><a href="#cite_note-fergie_time-228">[228]</a></sup> This was a greater figure than for other top clubs, although most of these clubs seem to benefit from a "Fergie Time" effect, particularly in their home matches.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fergie_time_228-1"><a href="#cite_note-fergie_time-228">[228]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy">Legacy</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sir_Alex_Ferguson_statue_at_Old_Trafford.jpg"><img alt="Sir Alex Ferguson statue at Old Trafford.jpg" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1934" data-file-width="1302" height="327" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Sir_Alex_Ferguson_statue_at_Old_Trafford.jpg/220px-Sir_Alex_Ferguson_statue_at_Old_Trafford.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Sir_Alex_Ferguson_statue_at_Old_Trafford.jpg/330px-Sir_Alex_Ferguson_statue_at_Old_Trafford.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Sir_Alex_Ferguson_statue_at_Old_Trafford.jpg/440px-Sir_Alex_Ferguson_statue_at_Old_Trafford.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sir_Alex_Ferguson_statue_at_Old_Trafford.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Sir Alex Ferguson statue installed at Old Trafford on 23 November 2012.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Many of Ferguson's former players have gone on to become football managers themselves, including <a href="/wiki/Tony_Fitzpatrick_(footballer)" title="Tony Fitzpatrick (footballer)">Tony Fitzpatrick</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alex_McLeish" title="Alex McLeish">Alex McLeish</a>, Gordon Strachan, <a href="/wiki/Mark_McGhee" title="Mark McGhee">Mark McGhee</a>, <a href="/wiki/Willie_Miller" title="Willie Miller">Willie Miller</a>, <a href="/wiki/Neale_Cooper" title="Neale Cooper">Neale Cooper</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bryan_Gunn" title="Bryan Gunn">Bryan Gunn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eric_Black" title="Eric Black">Eric Black</a>, <a href="/wiki/Billy_Stark" title="Billy Stark">Billy Stark</a>, Bryan Robson, Steve Bruce, Mark Hughes, Roy Keane, Paul Ince, <a href="/wiki/Chris_Casper" title="Chris Casper">Chris Casper</a>, Darren Ferguson, Ole Gunnar Solskjær, <a href="/wiki/Henning_Berg" title="Henning Berg">Henning Berg</a> and Gary Neville.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-229"><a href="#cite_note-229">[229]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-230"><a href="#cite_note-230">[230]</a></sup></p>
<p>The phrase "squeaky-bum time" coined by Ferguson in reference to the tense final stages of a league competition has been included in the <i><a href="/wiki/Collins_English_Dictionary" title="Collins English Dictionary">Collins English Dictionary</a></i> and the <i><a href="/wiki/Oxford_English_Dictionary" title="Oxford English Dictionary">Oxford English Dictionary</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-231"><a href="#cite_note-231">[231]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-232"><a href="#cite_note-232">[232]</a></sup></p>
<p>A bronze statue of Ferguson, designed by Scottish sculptor <a href="/wiki/Philip_Jackson_(sculptor)" title="Philip Jackson (sculptor)">Philip Jackson</a>, was unveiled outside Old Trafford on 23 November 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-233"><a href="#cite_note-233">[233]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-234"><a href="#cite_note-234">[234]</a></sup> On 14 October 2013, Ferguson attended a ceremony where a road near Old Trafford was renamed from Water's Reach to Sir Alex Ferguson Way.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-235"><a href="#cite_note-235">[235]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-236"><a href="#cite_note-236">[236]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span></h2>
<p>Ferguson lives in <a href="/wiki/Wilmslow" title="Wilmslow">Wilmslow</a>, Cheshire, with his wife, Cathy Ferguson (née Holding).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-237"><a href="#cite_note-237">[237]</a></sup> They married in 1966 and have three sons: Mark (born 1968); and twins <a href="/wiki/Darren_Ferguson" title="Darren Ferguson">Darren</a> (born 1972), former manager of <a href="/wiki/Peterborough_United_F.C." title="Peterborough United F.C.">Peterborough United</a> and former professional footballer; and Jason, who runs an events management company.</p>
<p>In 1998, Ferguson was named in a list of the biggest private financial donors to the <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Labour Party</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-238"><a href="#cite_note-238">[238]</a></sup> He is a self-described socialist<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-239"><a href="#cite_note-239">[239]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-240"><a href="#cite_note-240">[240]</a></sup> and a lifelong Labour voter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-241"><a href="#cite_note-241">[241]</a></sup> In January 2011 <a href="/wiki/Graham_Stringer" title="Graham Stringer">Graham Stringer</a>, a Labour MP in <a href="/wiki/Manchester" title="Manchester">Manchester</a> and Manchester United supporter, called for Ferguson to be made a <a href="/wiki/Life_peer" title="Life peer">life peer</a>. If this happened, it would make Ferguson the first current or former footballer or football manager to sit in the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Lords" title="House of Lords">House of Lords</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-242"><a href="#cite_note-242">[242]</a></sup> Stringer and fellow Manchester Labour MP <a href="/wiki/Paul_Goggins" title="Paul Goggins">Paul Goggins</a> repeated this call after Ferguson announced his retirement in May 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-243"><a href="#cite_note-243">[243]</a></sup> However, unnamed sources in the <i>Daily Mirror</i> newspaper claimed on 1 August 2013 that Ferguson had turned down a peerage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-244"><a href="#cite_note-244">[244]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2009, Ferguson received a Honorary Doctorate in Business Administration from the <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Metropolitan_University" title="Manchester Metropolitan University">Manchester Metropolitan University</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-245"><a href="#cite_note-245">[245]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-246"><a href="#cite_note-246">[246]</a></sup> It was the second degree he received from the university, after receiving a honorary masters in 1998.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-247"><a href="#cite_note-247">[247]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_independence_referendum,_2014" title="Scottish independence referendum, 2014">2014 Scottish independence referendum</a>, Ferguson was a vocal supporter and funder of the <a href="/wiki/Better_Together_(campaign)" title="Better Together (campaign)">Better Together</a> campaign that supported Scotland remaining a part of the United Kingdom.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-referendum_248-0"><a href="#cite_note-referendum-248">[248]</a></sup> He criticised the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_National_Party" title="Scottish National Party">Scottish National Party</a>, and its leader <a href="/wiki/Alex_Salmond" title="Alex Salmond">Alex Salmond</a>, for their decision to exclude Scots living outside Scotland, but within the rest of the United Kingdom, from voting in the referendum.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-referendum_248-1"><a href="#cite_note-referendum-248">[248]</a></sup> He also objected to the self-imposed rule by the <a href="/wiki/Yes_Scotland" title="Yes Scotland">Yes Scotland</a> group against accepting donations from people living outside Scotland of more than £500, which they urged the No campaign to also adopt.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-referendum_248-2"><a href="#cite_note-referendum-248">[248]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Honours">Honours</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Player">Player</span></h3>
<dl>
<dt>St Johnstone</dt>
</dl>
<ul>
<li>Scottish Football League Division 2 (2nd tier) (1): <a href="/wiki/1962%E2%80%9363_in_Scottish_football#Division_two" title="1962–63 in Scottish football">1962–63</a></li>
</ul>
<dl>
<dt>Falkirk</dt>
</dl>
<ul>
<li>Scottish Football League Division 2 (2nd tier) (1): <a href="/wiki/1969%E2%80%9370_in_Scottish_football#Division_two" title="1969–70 in Scottish football">1969–70</a></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Managerial">Managerial</span></h3>
<p>Ferguson was made an Inaugural Inductee of the <a href="/wiki/English_Football_Hall_of_Fame" title="English Football Hall of Fame">English Football Hall of Fame</a> in 2002 in recognition of his impact on the English game as a manager. In 2003, Ferguson became an inaugural recipient of the FA Coaching Diploma, awarded to all coaches who had at least ten years' experience of being a manager or head coach.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-249"><a href="#cite_note-249">[249]</a></sup> He is the Vice-President of the <a href="/wiki/National_Football_Museum" title="National Football Museum">National Football Museum</a>, based in <a href="/wiki/Manchester" title="Manchester">Manchester</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-250"><a href="#cite_note-250">[250]</a></sup> and a member of the Executive Committee of the <a href="/wiki/League_Managers_Association" title="League Managers Association">League Managers Association</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-251"><a href="#cite_note-251">[251]</a></sup> On 5 November 2011, the Old Trafford North Stand was officially renamed the <b>Sir Alex Ferguson Stand</b> in honour of his 25 years as manager of Manchester United.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-252"><a href="#cite_note-252">[252]</a></sup></p>
<p>In addition to being the only manager to win the top league honours, and the 'Double', north and south of the England–Scotland border (winning the Premier League with Manchester United, and the Scottish Premier Division with Aberdeen), he is also the last manager to win the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Scottish_football_champions" title="List of Scottish football champions">Scottish league championship</a> with a non <a href="/wiki/Old_Firm" title="Old Firm">Old Firm</a> team, achieving this in the <a href="/wiki/1984%E2%80%9385_in_Scottish_football" title="1984–85 in Scottish football">1984–85</a> season with <a href="/wiki/Aberdeen_F.C." title="Aberdeen F.C.">Aberdeen</a>. He is also the only manager in <a href="/wiki/Football_in_England" title="Football in England">English football</a> to have managed to finish in the top three league places in 20 consecutive seasons, since the <a href="/wiki/1991%E2%80%9392_Manchester_United_F.C._season" title="1991–92 Manchester United F.C. season">1991–92</a> season (with a total of 22 consecutive seasons).</p>
<p>Ferguson won 49 trophies as a manager, making him the most successful British football manager in history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-253"><a href="#cite_note-253">[253]</a></sup> He is also the <a href="/wiki/List_of_UEFA_club_competition_winning_managers" title="List of UEFA club competition winning managers">joint-most decorated manager</a> in European football competitions with seven honours, a record he shares with <a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Trapattoni" title="Giovanni Trapattoni">Giovanni Trapattoni</a> and <a href="/wiki/Carlo_Ancelotti" title="Carlo Ancelotti">Carlo Ancelotti</a>. Ferguson won the top division title in England a record 13 times, more than twice as many times as the next <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_English_football_championship_winning_managers" title="List of English football championship winning managers">most successful manager</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-254"><a href="#cite_note-254">[254]</a></sup> He is also the first manager in the history of the English league to win three consecutive league titles, which he did twice.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-255"><a href="#cite_note-255">[255]</a></sup> Ferguson won 10 manager of the year awards, 27 manager of the month awards and managed the most games in the UEFA Champions League (190).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-256"><a href="#cite_note-256">[256]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-257"><a href="#cite_note-257">[257]</a></sup> In 2017, Ferguson was named among the 10 most influential coaches since the foundation of <a href="/wiki/UEFA" title="UEFA">UEFA</a> in 1954.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-258"><a href="#cite_note-258">[258]</a></sup></p>

<dt>St Mirren</dt>
